<li><strong>What is a characteristic of a fault tolerant network?</strong>
<ul>
<li>a network that protects confidential information from unauthorized access</li>
<li>a network that can expand quickly to support new users and applications without impacting the performance of the service delivered to existing users</li>
<li>a network that supports a mechanism for managing congestion and ensuring reliable delivery of content to all users</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>a network that recovers quickly when a failure occurs and depends on redundancy to limit the impact of a failure*</strong></span></li>
</ul>
</li>

The second employee accesses the corporate database to perform some financial transactions. <ul>
<li>financial transactions, audio conference, web page</li>

<li>financial transactions, web page, audio conference</li>
</ul>

<ul>
<li>End users have the freedom to use personal tools to access information and communicate across a business network.</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>Network capabilities are extended without requiring investment in new infrastructure, personnel, or software.*</strong></span></li>
<li>Technology is integrated into every-day appliances allowing them to interconnect with other devices, making them more ‘smart’ or automated.</li>
<li>Home networking uses existing electrical wiring to connect devices to the network wherever there is an electrical outlet, saving the cost of installing data cables.</li>
</ul>

<li>192.168.10.0</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>192.168.10.128*</strong></span></li>
<li>192.168.10.192</li>
<li>192.168.10.224</li>
<li>192.168.10.240</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li><strong>Which statement is true about variable-length subnet masking?</strong>
<ul>
<li>Each subnet is the same size.</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>The size of each subnet may be different, depending on requirements.*</strong></span></li>
<li>Subnets may only be subnetted one additional time.</li>
<li>Bits are returned, rather than borrowed, to create additional subnets.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li><strong>In what two situations would UDP be the preferred transport protocol over TCP? (Choose two.)</strong>
<ul>
<li>when applications need to guarantee that a packet arrives intact, in sequence, and unduplicated</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>when a faster delivery mechanism is needed*</strong></span></li>
<li>when delivery overhead is not an issue</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>when applications do not need to guarantee delivery of the data*</strong></span></li>
<li>when destination port numbers are dynamic</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li><strong>What important information is added to the TCP/IP transport layer header to ensure communication and connectivity with a remote network device?</strong>
<ul>
<li>timing and synchronization</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>destination and source port numbers*</strong></span></li>
<li>destination and source physical addresses</li>
<li>destination and source logical network addresses</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li><strong>What is the TCP mechanism used in congestion avoidance?</strong>
<ul>
<li>three-way handshake</li>
<li>socket pair</li>
<li>two-way handshake</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>sliding window*</strong></span></li>
</ul>
</li>
<li><strong>Which scenario describes a function provided by the transport layer?</strong>
<ul>
<li>A student is using a classroom VoIP phone to call home. The unique identifier burned into the phone is a transport layer address used to contact another network device on the same network.</li>
<li>A student is playing a short web-based movie with sound. The movie and sound are encoded within the transport layer header.</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>A student has two web browser windows open in order to access two web sites. The transport layer ensures the correct web page is delivered to the correct browser window.*</strong></span></li>
<li>A corporate worker is accessing a web server located on a corporate network. The transport layer formats the screen so the web page appears properly no matter what device is being used to view the web site.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li><strong>A user opens three browsers on the same PC to access www.cisco.com to search for certification course information. The Cisco web server sends a datagram as a reply to the request from one of the web browsers. Which information is used by the TCP/IP protocol stack in the PC to identify which of the three web browsers should receive the reply?</strong>
<ul>
<li>the destination IP address</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>the destination port number*</strong></span></li>
<li>the source IP address</li>
<li>the source port number</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li><strong>What are two ways that TCP uses the sequence numbers in a segment? (Choose two.)</strong>
<ul>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>to identify missing segments at the destination *</strong></span></li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>to reassemble the segments at the remote location*</strong></span></li>
<li>to specify the order in which the segments travel from source to destination</li>
<li>to limit the number of segments that can be sent out of an interface at one time</li>
<li>to determine if the packet changed during transit</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li><strong>Which two tasks are functions of the presentation layer? (Choose two.)</strong>
<ul>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>compression*</strong></span></li>
<li>addressing</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>encryption*</strong></span></li>
<li>session control</li>
<li>authentication</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li><strong>Which three statements characterize UDP? (Choose three.)</strong>
<ul>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>UDP provides basic connectionless transport layer functions.*</strong></span></li>
<li>UDP provides connection-oriented, fast transport of data at Layer 3.</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>UDP relies on application layer protocols for error detection. *</strong></span></li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>UDP is a low overhead protocol that does not provide sequencing or flow control mechanisms.*</strong></span></li>
<li>UDP relies on IP for error detection and recovery.</li>
<li>UDP provides sophisticated flow control mechanisms.</li>
</ul>
</li>

</ul>

<li>Windows displays a DHCP timeout message.</li>

<li>The computer cannot ping other devices on the same network with IP addresses in the 169.254.0.0/16 range.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li><strong>Which command can an administrator issue on a Cisco router to send debug messages to the vty lines?</strong>
<ul>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>terminal monitor*</strong></span></li>
<li>logging console</li>
<li>logging buffered</li>
<li>logging synchronous</li>
</ul>
</li>

During data communications, a host may need to send a single message to a specific group of destination hosts simultaneously. This message is in the form of a <span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>Multicast *</strong></span>message.</li>

</ul>

<li><strong>What is the purpose of having a converged network?</strong>
<ul>
<li>to provide high speed connectivity to all end devices</li>
<li>to make sure that all types of data packets will be treated equally</li>
<li>to achieve fault tolerance and high availability of data network infrastructure devices</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>to reduce the cost of deploying and maintaining the communication infrastructure*</strong></span></li>
</ul>
</li>

<ul>
<li>reliability</li>

<li>quality of service</li>
<li>accessibility</li>
</ul>
</li>

<li><strong>Refer to the exhibit. From global configuration mode, an administrator is attempting to create a message-of-the-day banner by using the command banner motd V Authorized access only! Violators will be prosecuted! V When users log in using Telnet, the banner does not appear correctly. What is the problem?</strong><br>
<img src="./CCNA 1 Final Exam Answers 2018 (v5.1+v6.0) Introduction to Networks_files/36489.jpg"><p></p>
<ul>
<li>The banner message is too long.</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>The delimiting character appears in the banner message.*</strong></span></li>
<li>The symbol “!” signals the end of a banner message.</li>
<li>Message-of-the-day banners will only appear when a user logs in through the console port.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li><strong>What are three characteristics of an SVI? (Choose three.)</strong>
<ul>
<li>It is designed as a security protocol to protect switch ports.</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>It is not associated with any physical interface on a switch.*</strong></span></li>
<li>It is a special interface that allows connectivity by different types of media.</li>
<li>It is required to allow connectivity by any device at any location.</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>It provides a means to remotely manage a switch. *</strong></span></li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>It is associated with VLAN1 by default.*</strong></span></li>
</ul>
</li>
<li><strong>A technician configures a switch with these commands:</strong><strong>SwitchA(config)# interface vlan 1 </strong><br>
<strong>SwitchA(config-if)# ip address 192.168.1.1 255.255.255.0 </strong><br>
<strong>SwitchA(config-if)# no shutdown</strong><strong>What is the technician configuring?</strong><p></p>
<ul>
<li>Telnet access</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>SVI*</strong></span></li>
<li>password encryption</li>
<li>physical switchport access</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li><strong>In computer communication, what is the purpose of message encoding?</strong>
<ul>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>to convert information to the appropriate form for transmission*</strong></span></li>
<li>to interpret information</li>
<li>to break large messages into smaller frames</li>
<li>to negotiate correct timing for successful communication</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li><strong>What is a characteristic of multicast messages?</strong>
<ul>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>They are sent to a select group of hosts.*</strong></span></li>
<li>They must be acknowledged.</li>
<li>They are sent to a single destination.</li>
<li>They are sent to all hosts on a network.</li>
</ul>
</li>

<li><strong>How does a Layer 3 switch differ from a Layer 2 switch?</strong>
<ul>
<li>A Layer 3 switch supports VLANs, but a Layer 2 switch does not.</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>An IP address can be assigned to a physical port of a Layer 3 switch. However, this is not supported in Layer 2 switches.*</strong></span></li>
<li>A Layer 3 switch maintains an IP address table instead of a MAC address table.</li>
<li>A Layer 3 switch learns the MAC addresses that are associated with each of its ports. However, a Layer 2 switch does not.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li><strong>What is the purpose of the routing process?</strong>
<ul>
<li>to encapsulate data that is used to communicate across a network</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>to select the paths that are used to direct traffic to destination networks*</strong></span></li>
<li>to convert a URL name into an IP address</li>
<li>to provide secure Internet file transfer</li>
<li>to forward traffic on the basis of MAC addresses</li>
</ul>

<li><strong>Which three statements characterize the transport layer protocols? (Choose three.)</strong>
<ul>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>TCP and UDP port numbers are used by application layer protocols.*</strong></span></li>
<li>TCP uses port numbers to provide reliable transportation of IP packets.</li>
<li>UDP uses windowing and acknowledgments for reliable transfer of data.</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>TCP uses windowing and sequencing to provide reliable transfer of data.*</strong></span></li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>TCP is a connection-oriented protocol. UDP is a connectionless protocol.*</strong></span></li>
</ul>
</li>
<li><strong>Which statement is true regarding the UDP client process during a session with a server?</strong>
<ul>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>Datagrams that arrive in a different order than that in which they were sent are not placed in order.*</strong></span></li>
<li>A session must be established before datagrams can be exchanged.</li>
<li>A three-way handshake takes place before the transmission of data begins.</li>
<li>Application servers have to use port numbers above 1024 in order to be UDP capable.</li>
</ul>
</li>

<li><strong>What are two features of ARP? (Choose two.)</strong>
<ul>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>If a host is ready to send a packet to a local destination device and it has the IP address but not the MAC address of the destination, it generates an ARP broadcast.*</strong></span></li>
<li>An ARP request is sent to all devices on the Ethernet LAN and contains the IP address of the destination host and its multicast MAC address.</li>
<li>When a host is encapsulating a packet into a frame, it refers to the MAC address table to determine the mapping of IP addresses to MAC addresses.</li>
<li>If no device responds to the ARP request, then the originating node will broadcast the data packet to all devices on the network segment.</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>If a device receiving an ARP request has the destination IPv4 address, it responds with an ARP reply.*</strong></span></li>
</ul>
</li>

<li>An individual server can have two services that are assigned to the same port number.</li>
<li>An individual server cannot have multiple services running at the same time.</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>Server security can be improved by closing ports that are associated with unused services.*</strong></span></li>
</ul>

Although the cable has been cut, students in the dormitories only experience a very short interruption of network services. What characteristic of the network is shown here?</strong>

<li><strong>What is the function of the kernel of an operating software?</strong>
<ul>
<li>It provides a user interface that allows users to request a specific task.</li>
<li>The kernel links the hardware drivers with the underlying electronics of a computer.</li>
<li>It is an application that allows the initial configuration of a Cisco device.</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>The kernel provisions hardware resources to meet software requirements.*</strong></span></li>
</ul>
</li>
<p>
<div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
Operating systems function with a shell, a kernel, and the hardware. The shell interfaces with the users, allowing them to request specific tasks from the device. The kernel provisions resources from the hardware to meet software requirements. The hardware functions by using drivers and their underlying electronics. The hardware represents the physical components of the device.<br />
</p></div></li>
<p></p>
<li><strong>A network administrator needs to keep the user ID, password, and session contents private when establishing remote CLI connectivity with a switch to manage it. Which access method should be chosen?</strong>
<ul>
<li>Telnet</li>
<li>Console</li>
<li>AUX</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>SSH*</strong></span></li>
</ul>
</li>
<p>
<div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
To be truly private a technician would use a Console connection however if remote management is required SSH provides a secure method.<br />
</p></div></li>
<p></p>
<li><strong>Which procedure is used to access a Cisco 2960 switch when performing an initial configuration in a secure environment?</strong>
<ul>
<li>Use Telnet to remotely access the switch through the network.</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>Use the console port to locally access the switch from a serial or USB interface of the PC.*</strong></span></li>
<li>Use Secure Shell to remotely access the switch through the network.</li>
<li>Use the AUX port to locally access the switch from a serial or USB interface of the PC.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<p>
<div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
Telnet and SSH require active networking services to be configured on a Cisco device before they become functional. Cisco switches do not contain AUX ports.<br />
</p></div></li>
<p></p>
<li><strong>Which command or key combination allows a user to return to the previous level in the command hierarchy?</strong>
<ul>
<li>end</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>exit*</strong></span></li>
<li>Ctrl-Z</li>
<li>Ctrl-C</li>
</ul>
</li>
<p>
<div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
End and CTRL-Z return the user to the privileged EXEC mode. Ctrl-C ends a command in process. The exit command returns the user to the previous level.</p></div></li>
<p></p>
<li><strong>A router has a valid operating system and a configuration file stored in NVRAM. The configuration file contains an enable secret password but no console password. When the router boots up, which mode will display?</strong>
<ul>
<li>global configuration mode</li>
<li>setup mode</li>
<li>privileged EXEC mode</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>user EXEC mode *</strong></span></li>
</ul>
</li>
<p>
<div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
If a Cisco IOS device has a valid IOS and a valid configuration file, it will boot into user EXEC mode. A password will be required to enter privileged EXEC mode.<br />
</p></div></li>
<p></p>
<li><strong>Which two functions are provided to users by the context-sensitive help feature of the Cisco IOS CLI? (Choose two.)</strong>
<ul>
<li>providing an error message when a wrong command is submitted</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>displaying a list of all available commands within the current mode*</strong></span></li>
<li>allowing the user to complete the remainder of an abbreviated command with the TAB key</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>determining which option, keyword, or argument is available for the entered command*</strong></span></li>
<li>selecting the best command to accomplish a task</li>
</ul>
</li>
<p>
<div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
Context-sensitive help provides the user with a list of commands and the arguments associated with those commands within the current mode of a networking device. A syntax checker provides error checks on submitted commands and the TAB key can be used for command completion if a partial command is entered.<br />
</p></div></li>
<p></p>
<li><strong>Which information does the show startup-config command display?</strong>
<ul>
<li>the IOS image copied into RAM</li>
<li>the bootstrap program in the ROM</li>
<li>the contents of the current running configuration file in the RAM</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>the contents of the saved configuration file in the NVRAM *</strong></span></li>
</ul>
</li>
<p>
<div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
The show startup-config command displays the saved configuration located in NVRAM. The show running-config command displays the contents of the currently running configuration file located in RAM.​<br />
</p></div></li>

<li><strong>Why is it important to configure a hostname on a device?</strong>
<ul>
<li>a Cisco router or switch only begins to operate when its hostname is set</li>
<li>a hostname must be configured before any other parameters</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>to identify the device during remote access (SSH or telnet)*</strong></span></li>
<li>to allow local access to the device through the console port</li>
</ul>
</li>
<p>
<div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
It is important to configure a hostname because various authentication processes use the device hostname. Hostnames are helpful for documentation, and they identify the device during remote access.<br />
</p></div></li>

<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>RM-3-Switch-2A4*</strong></span></li>
<li>Floor(15)</li>
<li>HO Floor 17</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>SwBranch799*</strong></span></li>
</ul>
</li>
<p>
<div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
Some guidelines for naming conventions are that names should:<br />
Start with a letter<br />
Contain no spaces<br />
End with a letter or digit<br />
Use only letters, digits, and dashes<br />
Be less than 64 characters in length<br />
</p></div></li>
<p></p>
<li><strong>How does the service password-encryption command enhance password security on Cisco routers and switches?</strong>
<ul>
<li>It encrypts passwords as they are sent across the network.</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>It encrypts passwords that are stored in router or switch configuration files.*</strong></span></li>
<li>It requires that a user type encrypted passwords to gain console access to a router or switch.</li>
<li>It requires encrypted passwords to be used when connecting remotely to a router or switch with Telnet.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<p>
<div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
The service password-encryption command encrypts plaintext passwords in the configuration file so that they cannot be viewed by unauthorized users.<br />
</p></div></li>

<li><strong>Refer to the exhibit. A network administrator is configuring the MOTD on switch SW1. What is the purpose of this command?</strong><br />
<img src="https://ccnav6.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/05/i208238v1n2_208238.jpg" /></p>
<ul>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>to display a message when a user accesses the switch*</strong></span></li>
<li>to configure switch SW1 so that only the users in the Admin group can telnet into SW1</li>
<li>to force users of the Admin group to enter a password for authentication</li>
<li>to configure switch SW1 so that the message will display when a user enters the enable command</li>
</ul>
</li>
<p>
<div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
A banner message can be an important part of the legal process in the event that someone is prosecuted for breaking into a device. A banner message should make it clear that only authorized personnel should attempt to access the device. However, the banner command does not prevent unauthorized entry.<br />
</p></div></li>
<p></p>
<li><strong>While trying to solve a network issue, a technician made multiple changes to the current router configuration file. The changes did not solve the problem and were not saved. What action can the technician take to discard the changes and work with the file in NVRAM?</strong>
<ul>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>Issue the reload command without saving the running configuration.*</strong></span></li>
<li>Delete the vlan.dat file and reboot the device.</li>
<li>Close and reopen the terminal emulation software.</li>
<li>Issue the copy startup-config running-config command.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<p>
<div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
The technician does not want to make any mistakes trying to remove all the changes that were done to the running configuration file. The solution is to reboot the router without saving the running configuration. The copy startup-config running-config command does not overwrite the running configuration file with the configuration file stored in NVRAM, but rather it just has an additive effect.<br />
</p></div></li>
<p></p>
<li><strong>What is the function of the kernel of an operating system?</strong>
<ul>
<li>It provides a user interface that allows users to request a specific task.</li>
<li>The kernel links the hardware drivers with the underlying electronics of a computer.</li>
<li>It is an application that allows the initial configuration of a Cisco device.</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>The kernel provisions hardware resources to meet software requirements.*</strong></span></li>
</ul>
</li>
<p>
<div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
Operating systems function with a shell, a kernel, and the hardware. The shell interfaces with the users, allowing them to request specific tasks from the device. The kernel provisions resources from the hardware to meet software requirements. The hardware functions by using drivers and their underlying electronics. The hardware represents the physical components of the device.</p></div></li>
<p></p>
<li><strong>A router with a valid operating system contains a configuration file stored in NVRAM. The configuration file has an enable secret password but no console password. When the router boots up, which mode will display?</strong>
<ul>
<li>privileged EXEC mode</li>
<li>setup mode</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>user EXEC mode*</strong></span></li>
<li>global configuration mode</li>
</ul>
</li>
<p>
<div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong>If a Cisco IOS device has a valid IOS and a valid configuration file, it will boot into user EXEC mode. A password will be required to enter privileged EXEC mode.</p></div></li>

<p></p>
<li><strong>Which statement is true about the running configuration file in a Cisco IOS device?</strong>
<ul>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>It affects the operation of the device immediately when modified.*</strong></span></li>
<li>It is stored in NVRAM.</li>
<li>It should be deleted using the erase running-config command.</li>
<li>It is automatically saved when the router reboots.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<p>
<div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
As soon as configuration commands are entered into a router, they modify the device immediately. Running configuration files can not be deleted nor are they saved automatically.<br />
</p></div></li>
<p></p>
<li><strong>What are two characteristics of RAM on a Cisco device? (Choose two.)</strong>
<ul>
<li>RAM provides nonvolatile storage.</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>The configuration that is actively running on the device is stored in RAM. *</strong></span></li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>The contents of RAM are lost during a power cycle. *</strong></span></li>
<li>RAM is a component in Cisco switches but not in Cisco routers.</li>
<li>RAM is able to store multiple versions of IOS and configuration files.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<p>
<div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
RAM stores data that is used by the device to support network operations. The running configuration is stored in RAM. This type of memory is considered volatile memory because data is lost during a power cycle. Flash memory stores the IOS and delivers a copy of the IOS into RAM when a device is powered on. Flash memory is nonvolatile since it retains stored contents during a loss of power.<br />
</p></div></li>
<p></p>
<li><strong>Which interface allows remote management of a Layer 2 switch?</strong>
<ul>
<li>the AUX interface</li>
<li>the console port interface</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>the switch virtual interface*</strong></span></li>
<li>the first Ethernet port interface</li>
</ul>
</li>
<p>
<div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
In a Layer 2 switch, there is a switch virtual interface (SVI) that provides a means for remotely managing the device.<br />
</p></div></li>
<p></p>
<li><strong>Which interface is the default SVI on a Cisco switch?</strong>
<ul>
<li>FastEthernet 0/1</li>
<li>GigabitEthernet 0/1</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>VLAN 1*</strong></span></li>
<li>VLAN 99</li>
</ul>
</li>
<p>
<div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
An SVI is a virtual interface and VLAN 1 is enabled by default on Cisco switches. VLAN 99 must be configured to be used. FastEthernet 0/1 and GigabitEthernet 0/1 are physical interfaces.<br />
</p></div></li>
<p></p>
<li><strong>Why would a Layer 2 switch need an IP address?</strong>
<ul>
<li>to enable the switch to send broadcast frames to attached PCs</li>
<li>to enable the switch to function as a default gateway</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>to enable the switch to be managed remotely*</strong></span></li>
<li>to enable the switch to receive frames from attached PCs</li>
</ul>
</li>
<p>
<div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
A switch, as a Layer 2 device, does not need an IP address to transmit frames to attached devices. However, when a switch is accessed remotely through the network, it must have a Layer 3 address. The IP address must be applied to a virtual interface rather than to a physical interface. Routers, not switches, function as default gateways.<br />
</p></div></li>
<p></p>
<li><strong>What command can be used on a Windows PC to see the IP configuration of that computer?</strong>
<ul>
<li>ping</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>ipconfig*</strong></span></li>
<li>show interfaces</li>
<li>show ip interface brief</li>
</ul>
</li>
<p>
<div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
On a Windows PC, the ipconfig command can be used to verify the current IP configuration. The ping command can be used to verify connectivity to other network devices. The show interfaces and show ip interface brief commands are both Cisco IOS commands that are used to see the status of router and switch interfaces.<br />
</p></div></li>
<p></p>
<li><strong>A technician is adding a new PC to a LAN. After unpacking the components and making all the connections, the technician starts the PC. After the OS loads, the technician opens a browser, and verifies that the PC can reach the Internet. Why was the PC able to connect to the network with no additional configuration?</strong>
<ul>
<li>The PC does not require any additional information to function on the network.</li>
<li>The PC came preconfigured with IP addressing information from the factory.</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>The PC was preconfigured to use DHCP.*</strong></span></li>
<li>The PC used DNS to automatically receive IP addressing information from a server.</li>
<li>The PC virtual interface is compatible with any network.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<p>
<div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
The new PC was preconfigured to use DHCP. When the PC is connected to a network that uses DHCP, it gets the IP address settings from the DHCP server that will allow it to function on the network. All devices require at least an IP address and subnet mask to function on a LAN. DNS does not automatically configure addresses on hosts. PC virtual interfaces are not universally compatible with LANs and do not necessarily provide a host with an IP address. At this place in the course, virtual interfaces are used on network switches.<br />
</p></div></li>
<p></p>
<li><strong>What is a user trying to determine when issuing a ping 10.1.1.1 command on a PC?</strong>
<ul>
<li>if the TCP/IP stack is functioning on the PC without putting traffic on the wire</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>if there is connectivity with the destination device*</strong></span></li>
<li>the path that traffic will take to reach the destination</li>
<li>what type of device is at the destination</li>
</ul>
</li>
<p>
<div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
The ping destination command can be used to test connectivity.<br />
</p></div></li>
<p></p>
<li><strong>Refer to the exhibit. A network technician is testing connectivity in a new network. Based on the test results shown in the exhibit, which device does the technician have connectivity with and which device does the technician not have connectivity with? (Choose two.)</strong><br />
<img src="https://ccnav6.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/05/i274052v1n3_274052.jpg" /></p>
<ul>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>connectivity: switch 2*</strong></span></li>
<li>connectivity: PC-D</li>
<li>connectivity: PC-B</li>
<li>no connectivity: switch 1</li>
<li>no connectivity: switch 2</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>no connectivity: PC-C*</strong></span></li>
</ul>
</li>
<p>
<div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
The exhibit shows ping tests to two devices. One device has the IP address of 192.168.1.2, which is switch 2. The other test is to the IP address of 192.168.1.21, which is host PC-C. For the first test, to switch 2, the results are successful, with four reply messages received. This means that connectivity exists to switch 2. For the second test, all four messages timed out. This indicates that connectivity does not exist to PC-C.<br />
</p></div></li>

<li><strong>Refer to the exhibit.</strong><br />
<img src="https://ccnav6.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/05/i274067v1n1_274067.jpg" /><br />
<strong>Refer to the exhibit. What three facts can be determined from the viewable output of the show ip interface brief command? (Choose three.)</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>Two physical interfaces have been configured.</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>The switch can be remotely managed.*</strong></span></li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>One device is attached to a physical interface.*</strong></span></li>
<li>Passwords have been configured on the switch.</li>
<li>Two devices are attached to the switch.</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>The default SVI has been configured.*</strong></span></li>
</ul>
</li>

Vlan1 is the default SVI. Because an SVI has been configured, the switch can be configured and managed remotely. FastEthernet0/0 is showing up and up, so a device is connected.<br />
</p></div></li>

<li><strong>An administrator is configuring a switch console port with a password. In what order will the administrator travel through the IOS modes of operation in order to reach the mode in which the configuration commands will be entered? (Not all options are used.)</strong><br />
<img src="https://ccnav6.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/05/2017-05-22_141306.jpg" /><br />
<img class="aligncenter size-full wp-image-8829" src="https://ccnav6.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/03/2017-05-26_100439-1.png" alt="" width="927" height="219" srcset="https://ccnav6.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/03/2017-05-26_100439-1.png 927w, https://ccnav6.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/03/2017-05-26_100439-1-300x71.png 300w, https://ccnav6.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/03/2017-05-26_100439-1-768x181.png 768w" sizes="(max-width: 927px) 100vw, 927px" /><br />
<strong>Place the options in the following order:</strong><br />
&#8211; not scored &#8211;<br />
second mode<br />
final mode<br />
third mode<br />
first mode<br />
<div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
The configuration mode that the administrator first encounters is user EXEC mode. After the enable command is entered, the next mode is privileged EXEC mode. From there, the configure terminal command is entered to move to global configuration mode. Finally, the administrator enters the line console 0 command to enter the mode in which the configuration will be entered.<br />
</p></div></li>
<p></p>
<li><strong>Match the definitions to their respective CLI hot keys and shortcuts. (Not all options are used.)</strong><br />
<strong>Question</strong><br />
<img src="https://ccnav6.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/05/2017-05-22_141638.jpg" /><br />
<strong>Answer</strong><br />
<img class="aligncenter size-full wp-image-8830" src="https://ccnav6.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/03/2017-05-26_101146.png" alt="" width="932" height="254" srcset="https://ccnav6.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/03/2017-05-26_101146.png 932w, https://ccnav6.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/03/2017-05-26_101146-300x82.png 300w, https://ccnav6.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/03/2017-05-26_101146-768x209.png 768w" sizes="(max-width: 932px) 100vw, 932px" /><br />
<strong>Place the options in the following order: </strong><br />
completes abbreviated commands and parameters<br />
displays the next screen<br />
scrolls backwards through previously entered commands<br />
&#8211; not scored &#8211;<br />
provides context-sensitive help<br />
aborts commands such as trace and ping<br />
<div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
The shortcuts with their functions are as follows:<br />
&#8211; Tab &#8211; Completes the remainder of a partially typed command or keyword<br />
&#8211; Space bar &#8211; displays the next screen<br />
&#8211; ? &#8211; provides context-sensitive help<br />
&#8211; Up Arrow &#8211; Allows user to scroll backward through former commands<br />
&#8211; Ctrl-C &#8211; cancels any command currently being entered and returns directly to privileged EXEC mode<br />
&#8211; Ctrl-Shift-6 &#8211; Allows the user to interrupt an IOS process such as ping or traceroute<br />
</p></div>
</li>

<ul>
<li>Are the devices on the same LAN?</li>
<li>Do the devices have enough NVRAM to store the IOS image?</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>What models of routers and switches require upgrades?*</strong></span></li>
<li>What ports are installed on the routers and switches?</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>Do the routers and switches have enough RAM and flash memory for the proposed IOS versions? *</strong></span></li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>What features are required for the devices?*</strong></span></li>
</ul>
</li>

<li>What is a result of using the service password-encryption command on a Cisco network device?</strong>
<ul>
<li>The command encrypts the banner message.</li>
<li>The command encrypts the enable mode password.</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>All passwords in the configuration are not shown in clear text when viewing the configuration.*</strong></span></li>
<li>A network administrator who later logs into the device will be required to enter an administrator password in order to gain access to the Cisco device.</li>
</ul>
</li>

<ul>
<li>Reboot the device.</li>
<li>Enter CTRL-Z at the privileged mode prompt.</li>
<li>Exit global configuration mode.</li>
<li>Power cycle the device.</li>

</ul>

<strong></p>
<li>What benefit does DHCP provide to a network?</strong>
<ul>
<li>Hosts always have the same IP address and are therefore always reachable.</li>
<li>DHCP allows users to refer to locations by a name rather than an IP address.</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>Hosts can connect to the network and get an IP address without manual configuration.*</strong></span></li>
<li>Duplicate addresses cannot occur on a network that issues dynamic addresses using DHCP and has static assignments.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<p>
<strong></p>
<li>What criterion must be followed in the design of an IPv4 addressing scheme for end devices?</strong>
<ul>
<li>Each IP address must match the address that is assigned to the host by DNS.</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>Each IP address must be unique within the local network.*</strong></span></li>
<li>Each IP address needs to be compatible with the MAC address.</li>
<li>Each local host should be assigned an IP address with a unique network component.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<p>
<strong></p>
<li>Refer to the exhibit. A switch was configured as shown. A ping to the default gateway was issued, but the ping was not successful. Other switches in the same network can ping this gateway. What is a possible reason for this?</strong><br />
<img src="https://ccnav6.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/05/i204793v1n1_204793.png" /></p>
<ul>
<li>The VLAN IP address and the default gateway IP address are not in the same network.</li>
<li>The local DNS server is not functioning correctly.</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>The no shutdown command was not issued for VLAN 1.*</strong></span></li>
<li>The ip default-gateway command has to be issued in the VLAN interface configuration mode.</li>
<li>The default gateway address must be 192.168.10.1.</li>
</ul>
</li>

<li><strong>Which two features are characteristics of flash memory? (Choose two.)</strong><br />
Flash receives a copy of the IOS from RAM when a device is powered on.<br />
<span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>Flash provides nonvolatile storage.*</strong></span><br />
<span style="color: #ff0000;"> <strong>The contents of flash may be overwritten.*</strong></span><br />
Flash is a component in Cisco switches but not in Cisco routers.<br />
The contents of flash may be lost during a power cycle.
</li>

<li><strong>Match the description to the common IOS CLI access method.</strong><br />
<img class="aligncenter size-full wp-image-6850" src="https://ccnav6.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/03/p20-exa2-ccna1.png" alt="" width="759" height="415" srcset="https://ccnav6.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/03/p20-exa2-ccna1.png 759w, https://ccnav6.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/03/p20-exa2-ccna1-300x164.png 300w" sizes="(max-width: 759px) 100vw, 759px" /><br />
<strong>Console port</strong><br />
<span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>It displays startup, debugging, and error messages by default.*</strong></span><br />
<span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>It can be used to restore an out-of-box configuration on a switch or router.*</strong></span><br />
<strong>Virtual interface</strong><br />
<span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>It allows access throught use of Telnet or SSH protocols.*</strong></span><br />
<span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>It requires an active network connection.*</strong></span><br />
<strong>AUX port</strong><br />
<span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>It connects throught dialup connections*</strong></span><br />
<span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>It is not supported on Catalyst switch devices*</strong></span>
</li>

<!-- 3 chapter -->

<li><strong>What method can be used by two computers to ensure that packets are not dropped because too much data is being sent too quickly?</strong>
<ul>
<li>encapsulation</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>flow control*</strong></span></li>
<li>access method</li>
<li>response timeout</li>
</ul>
<p><div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
In order for two computers to be able to communicate effectively, there must be a mechanism that allows both the source and destination to set the timing of the transmission and receipt of data. Flow control allows for this by ensuring that data is not sent too fast for it to be received properly.</p></div></li>
<li><strong>What type of communication will send a message to all devices on a local area network?</strong>
<ul>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>broadcast*</strong></span></li>
<li>multicast</li>
<li>unicast</li>
<li>allcast</li>
</ul>
<p><div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong>Broadcast communication is a one-to-all communication. A unicast communication is a one-to-one communication. Multicast is a one-to-many communication where the message is delivered to a specific group of hosts. Allcast is not a standard term to describe message delivery.</p></div></li>
<li><strong>What process is used to place one message inside another message for transfer from the source to the destination?</strong>
<ul>
<li>access control</li>
<li>decoding</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>encapsulation*</strong></span></li>
<li>flow control</li>
</ul>
<p><div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong>Encapsulation is the process of placing one message format into another message format. An example is how a packet is placed in its entirety into the data field as it is encapsulated into a frame.<br />
</p></div></li>
<li><strong>A web client is sending a request for a webpage to a web server. From the perspective of the client, what is the correct order of the protocol stack that is used to prepare the request for transmission?</strong>
<ul>
<li>HTTP, IP, TCP, Ethernet</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>HTTP, TCP, IP, Ethernet*</strong></span></li>
<li>Ethernet, TCP, IP, HTTP</li>
<li>Ethernet, IP, TCP, HTTP</li>
</ul>
<p><div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
1. HTTP governs the way that a web server and client interact.<br />
2. TCP manages individual conversations between web servers and clients.<br />
3. IP is responsible for delivery across the best path to the destination.<br />
4. Ethernet takes the packet from IP and formats it for transmission.<br />
</p></div></li>
<li><strong>Which statement is correct about network protocols?</strong>
<ul>
<li>Network protocols define the type of hardware that is used and how it is mounted in racks.</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>They define how messages are exchanged between the source and the destination.*</strong></span></li>
<li>They all function in the network access layer of TCP/IP.</li>
<li>They are only required for exchange of messages between devices on remote networks.</li>
</ul>
<p><div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
Network protocols are implemented in hardware, or software, or both. They interact with each other within different layers of a protocol stack. Protocols have nothing to do with the installation of the network equipment. Network protocols are required to exchange information between source and destination devices in both local and remote networks.<br />
</p></div></li>
<li><strong>Which statement is true about the TCP/IP and OSI models?</strong>
<ul>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>The TCP/IP transport layer and OSI Layer 4 provide similar services and functions.*</strong></span></li>
<li>The TCP/IP network access layer has similar functions to the OSI network layer.</li>
<li>The OSI Layer 7 and the TCP/IP application layer provide identical functions.</li>
<li>The first three OSI layers describe general services that are also provided by the TCP/IP internet layer.</li>
</ul>
<p><div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
he TCP/IP internet layer provides the same function as the OSI network layer. The transport layer of both the TCP/IP and OSI models provides the same function. The TCP/IP application layer includes the same functions as OSI Layers 5, 6, and 7.<br />
</p></div></li>
<li><strong>What is an advantage of using standards to develop and implement protocols?</strong>
<ul>
<li>A particular protocol can only be implemented by one manufacturer.</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>Products from different manufacturers can interoperate successfully.*</strong></span></li>
<li>Different manufacturers are free to apply different requirements when implementing a protocol.</li>
<li>Standards provide flexibility for manufacturers to create devices that comply with unique requirements.</li>
</ul>
<p><div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
Standards-based protocols enable products from different manufacturers to interoperate successfully. Standards-based protocols enable many manufacturers to implement that protocol. If different manufacturers implement different requirements within the same protocol, then their products will not be interoperable.<br />
</p></div></li>
<li><strong>What three application layer protocols are part of the TCP/IP protocol suite? (Choose three.)</strong>
<ul>
<li>ARP</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>DHCP *</strong></span></li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>DNS *</strong></span></li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>FTP*</strong></span></li>
<li>NAT</li>
<li>PPP</li>
</ul>
<p><div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
DNS, DHCP, and FTP are all application layer protocols in the TCP/IP protocol suite. ARP and PPP are network access layer protocols, and NAT is an internet layer protocol in the TCP/IP protocol suite.<br />
</p></div></li>
<li><strong>What are proprietary protocols?</strong>
<ul>
<li>protocols developed by private organizations to operate on any vendor hardware</li>
<li>protocols that can be freely used by any organization or vendor</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>protocols developed by organizations who have control over their definition and operation*</strong></span></li>
<li>a collection of protocols known as the TCP/IP protocol suite</li>
</ul>
<p><div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
Proprietary protocols have their definition and operation controlled by one company or vendor. Some of them can be used by different organizations with permission from the owner. The TCP/IP protocol suite is an open standard, not a proprietary protocol.<br />
</p></div></li>
<li><strong>What is an advantage of network devices using open standard protocols?</strong>
<ul>
<li>Network communications is confined to data transfers between devices from the same vendor.</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>A client host and a server running different operating systems can successfully exchange data.*</strong></span></li>
<li>Internet access can be controlled by a single ISP in each market.</li>
<li>Competition and innovation are limited to specific types of products.</li>
</ul>
<p><div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
An advantage of network devices implementing open standard protocols, such as from the TCP/IP suite, is that clients and servers running different operating systems can communicate with each other. Open standard protocols facilitate innovation and competition between vendors and across markets, and can reduce the occurrence of monopolies in networking markets.<br />
</p></div></li>
<li><strong>Refer to the exhibit. If Host1 were to transfer a file to the server, what layers of the TCP/IP model would be used?</strong><br />
<img src="https://ccnav6.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/05/i275370v1n1_275370.jpg" /></p>
<ul>
<li>only application and Internet layers</li>
<li>only Internet and network access layers</li>
<li>only application, Internet, and network access layers</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>application, transport, Internet, and network access layers*</strong></span></li>
<li>only application, transport, network, data link, and physical layers</li>
<li>application, session, transport, network, data link, and physical layers</li>
</ul>
<p><div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
The TCP/IP model contains the application, transport, internet, and network access layers. A file transfer uses the FTP application layer protocol. The data would move from the application layer through all of the layers of the model and across the network to the file server.<br />
</p></div></li>
<li><strong>Which three layers of the OSI model are comparable in function to the application layer of the TCP/IP model? (Choose three.)</strong>
<ul>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong> application *</strong></span></li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>presentation *</strong></span></li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>session*</strong></span></li>
<li>transport</li>
<li>data link</li>
<li>physical</li>
<li>network</li>
</ul>
<p><div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
The TCP/IP model consists of four layers: application, transport, internet, and network access. The OSI model consists of seven layers: application, presentation, session, transport, network, data link, and physical. The top three layers of the OSI model: application, presentation, and session map to the application layer of the TCP/IP model.<br />
</p></div></li>
<li><strong>At which layer of the OSI model would a logical address be encapsulated?</strong>
<ul>
<li>physical layer</li>
<li>data link layer</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>network layer*</strong></span></li>
<li>transport layer</li>
</ul>
<p><div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
Logical addresses, also known as IP addresses, are encapsulated at the network layer. Physical addresses are encapsulated at the data link layer. Port addresses are encapsulated at the transport layer. No addresses are encapsulated at the physical layer.<br />
</p></div></li>
<li><strong>At which layer of the OSI model would a logical address be added during encapsulation??</strong>
<ul>
<li>physical layer</li>
<li>data link layer</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>network layer*</strong></span></li>
<li>transport layer</li>
</ul>
<p><div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
Logical addresses, also known as IP addresses, are encapsulated at the network layer. Physical addresses are encapsulated at the data link layer. Port addresses are encapsulated at the transport layer. No addresses are encapsulated at the physical layer.<br />
</p></div></li>
<li><strong>Which PDU format is used when bits are received from the network medium by the NIC of a host?</strong>
<ul>
<li>file</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>frame*</strong></span></li>
<li>packet</li>
<li>segment</li>
</ul>
<p><div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
When received at the physical layer of a host, the bits are formatted into a frame at the data link layer. A packet is the PDU at the network layer. A segment is the PDU at the transport layer. A file is a data structure that may be used at the application layer.<br />
</p></div></li>
<li><strong>Which PDU is processed when a host computer is de-encapsulating a message at the transport layer of the TCP/IP model?</strong>
<ul>
<li>bits</li>
<li>frame</li>
<li>packet</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>segment*</strong></span></li>
</ul>
<p><div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
At the transport layer, a host computer will de-encapsulate a segment to reassemble data to an acceptable format by the application layer protocol of the TCP/IP model.<br />
</p></div></li>
<li><strong>Refer to the exhibit. HostA is attempting to contact ServerB. Which two statements correctly describe the addressing that HostA will generate in the process? (Choose two.)</strong><br />
<img src="https://ccnav6.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/05/i214638v1n1_214638.jpg" /></p>
<ul>
<li>A packet with the destination IP address of RouterB.</li>
<li>A frame with the destination MAC address of SwitchA.</li>
<li>A packet with the destination IP address of RouterA.</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>A frame with the destination MAC address of RouterA.*</strong></span></li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>A packet with the destination IP address of ServerB.*</strong></span></li>
<li>A frame with the destination MAC address of ServerB.</li>
</ul>
<p><div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
In order to send data to ServerB, HostA will generate a packet that contains the IP address of the destination device on the remote network and a frame that contains the MAC address of the default gateway device on the local network.</p></div></li>
<li><strong>Which address does a NIC use when deciding whether to accept a frame?</strong>
<ul>
<li>source IP address</li>
<li>source MAC address</li>
<li>destination IP address</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>destination MAC address*</strong></span></li>
<li>source Ethernet address</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li><strong>What will happen if the default gateway address is incorrectly configured on a host?</strong>
<ul>
<li>The host cannot communicate with other hosts in the local network.</li>
<li>The switch will not forward packets initiated by the host.</li>
<li>The host will have to use ARP to determine the correct address of the default gateway.</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>The host cannot communicate with hosts in other networks.*</strong></span></li>
<li>A ping from the host to 127.0.0.1 would not be successful.</li>
</ul>
<p><div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
When a host needs to send a message to another host located on the same network, it can forward the message directly. However, when a host needs to send a message to a remote network, it must use the router, also known as the default gateway. This is because the data link frame address of the remote destination host cannot be used directly. Instead, the IP packet has to be sent to the router (default gateway) and the router will forward the packet toward its destination. Therefore, if the default gateway is incorrectly configured, the host can communicate with other hosts on the same network, but not with hosts on remote networks.<br />
</p></div></li>
<li><strong>Which characteristic describes the default gateway of a host computer?</strong>
<ul>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>the logical address of the router interface on the same network as the host computer*</strong></span></li>
<li>the physical address of the switch interface connected to the host computer</li>
<li>the physical address of the router interface on the same network as the host computer</li>
<li>the logical address assigned to the switch interface connected to the router</li>
</ul>
<p><div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
The default gateway is the IP address of an interface on the router on the same network as the sending host.<br />
</p></div></li>

<li><strong>Match the protocol function to the description while taking into consideration that a network client is visiting a web site. (Not all options are used.)</strong><br />
<img src="https://ccnav6.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/05/2017-05-23_190732.png" alt="" /><br />
<img class="aligncenter size-full wp-image-8834" src="https://ccnav6.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/03/2017-05-26_104312.png" alt="" width="918" height="278" srcset="https://ccnav6.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/03/2017-05-26_104312.png 918w, https://ccnav6.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/03/2017-05-26_104312-300x91.png 300w, https://ccnav6.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/03/2017-05-26_104312-768x233.png 768w" sizes="(max-width: 918px) 100vw, 918px" /><br />
<strong>Place the options in the following order: </strong><br />
<strong><span style="color: #ff0000;">governing the way a web server and a web client interact</span></strong> &#8211;&gt; application protocol<br />
<strong><span style="color: #ff0000;">taking the segments from transport protocol, encapsulating them into packets, and assigning them with appropriate addresses</span></strong> &#8211;&gt; internet protocol<br />
<strong><span style="color: #ff0000;">preparing packets to be transmitted over the network media</span></strong> &#8211;&gt; network access protocol<br />
&#8211; not scored &#8211;<br />
<strong><span style="color: #ff0000;">managing the individual conversations between web servers and web clients</span></strong> &#8211;&gt; transport protocol<br />
<div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
When a web client visits a web server, several network communication protocols are involved. These different protocols work together to ensure that the messages are received and understood by both parties. These protocols include the following:<br />
Application Protocol &#8211; governing the way a web server and a web client interact<br />
Transport Protocol &#8211; managing the individual conversations between web servers and web clients<br />
Internet Protocol &#8211; taking the formatted segments from the transport protocol, encapsulating them into packets, assigning them the appropriate addresses, and delivering them across the best path to the destination host<br />
Network Access Protocol &#8211; preparing packets to be transmitted over the network media<br />
Network Time Protocol is used to synchronize clocks between computer systems. It is not involved in this case.<br />
</p></div></li>
<li><strong>Match each description to its corresponding term. (Not all options are used.)</strong><br />
<img src="https://ccnav6.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/05/2017-05-23_190456.png" alt="" /><br />

<strong><span style="color: #ff0000;">message encoding</span></strong> -&gt; the process of converting information from one format into another acceptable for transmission<br />
<strong><span style="color: #ff0000;">message encapsulation</span></strong> -&gt; the process of placing one message format inside another message format<br />
&#8211; not scored &#8211;<br />
<strong><span style="color: #ff0000;">message sizing</span></strong> -&gt; the process of breaking up a long message into individual pieces before being sent over the network</li>
