<li><strong>What are two reasons for physical layer protocols to use frame encoding techniques? (Choose two.)</strong>
<ul>
<li>to reduce the number of collisions on the media</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>to distinguish data bits from control bits*</strong></span></li>
<li>to provide better media error correction</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>to identify where the frame starts and ends*</strong></span></li>
<li>to increase the media throughput</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>to distinguish data from control information*</strong></span></li>
</ul>
<p><div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
An encoding technique converts a stream of data bits in a predefined code that can be recognized by both the transmitter and the receiver. Using predefined patterns helps to differentiate data bits from control bits and provide better media error detection.<br />
</p></div></li>
<li><strong>What is indicated by the term throughput?</strong>
<ul>
<li>the guaranteed data transfer rate offered by an ISP</li>
<li>the capacity of a particular medium to carry data</li>
<li>the measure of the usable data transferred across the media</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>the measure of the bits transferred across the media over a given period of time*</strong></span></li>
<li>the time it takes for a message to get from sender to receiver</li>
</ul>
<p><div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
Throughput is the measure of the transfer of bits across the media over a given period of time. Throughput is affected by a number of factors such as, EMI and latency, so it rarely matches the specified bandwidth for a network medium. The throughput measurement includes user data bits and other data bits, such as overhead, acknowledging, and encapsulation. The measure of the usable data transferred across the media is called goodput.<br />
</p></div></li>
<li><strong>A network administrator notices that some newly installed Ethernet cabling is carrying corrupt and distorted data signals. The new cabling was installed in the ceiling close to fluorescent lights and electrical equipment. Which two factors may interfere with the copper cabling and result in signal distortion and data corruption? (Choose two.)</strong>
<ul>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>EMI*</strong></span></li>
<li>crosstalk</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>RFI*</strong></span></li>
<li>signal attenuation</li>
<li>extended length of cabling</li>
</ul>
<p><div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
EMI and RFI signals can distort and corrupt data signals that are carried by copper media. These distortions usually come from radio waves and electromagnetic devices such as motors and florescent lights. Crosstalk is a disturbance that is caused by adjacent wires bundled too close together with the magnetic field of one wire affecting another. Signal attenuation is caused when an electrical signal begins to deteriorate over the length of a copper cable.<br />
</p></div></li>
<li><strong>Which characteristic describes crosstalk?</strong>
<ul>
<li>the distortion of the network signal from fluorescent lighting</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>the distortion of the transmitted messages from signals carried in adjacent wires*</strong></span></li>
<li>the weakening of the network signal over long cable lengths</li>
<li>the loss of wireless signal over excessive distance from the access point</li>
</ul>
<p><div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
EMI and RFI can distort network signals because of interference from fluorescent lights or electric motors. Attenuation results in deterioration of the network signal as it travels along copper cabling. Wireless devices can experience loss of signals because of excessive distances from a access point, but this is not crosstalk. Crosstalk is the disturbance caused by the electric or magnetic fields of the signal carried on an adjacent wire within the same cable.<br />
</p></div></li>
<li><strong>What technique is used with UTP cable to help protect against signal interference from crosstalk?</strong>
<ul>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>twisting the wires together into pairs*</strong></span></li>
<li>wrapping a foil shield around the wire pairs</li>
<li>encasing the cables within a flexible plastic sheath</li>
<li>terminating the cable with special grounded connectors</li>
</ul>
<p><div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
To help prevent the effects of crosstalk, UTP cable wires are twisted together into pairs. Twisting the wires together causes the magnetic fields of each wire to cancel each other out.<br />
</p></div></li>
<li><strong>Refer to the exhibit. The PC is connected to the console port of the switch. All the other connections are made through FastEthernet links. Which types of UTP cables can be used to connect the devices?</strong><br />
<img src="https://ccnav6.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/05/i274301v1n1_206934.jpg" /></p>
<ul>
<li>1 – rollover, 2 – crossover, 3 – straight-through</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>1 – rollover, 2 – straight-through, 3 – crossover*</strong></span></li>
<li>1 – crossover, 2 – straight-through, 3 – rollover</li>
<li>1 – crossover, 2 – rollover, 3 – straight-through</li>
</ul>
<p><div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
A straight-through cable is commonly used to interconnect a host to a switch and a switch to a router. A crossover cable is used to interconnect similar devices together like switch to a switch, a host to a host, or a router to a router. If a switch has the MDIX capability, a crossover could be used to connect the switch to the router; however, that option is not available. A rollover cable is used to connect to a router or switch console port.<br />
</p></div></li>
<li><strong>Refer to the exhibit. What is wrong with the displayed termination?</strong><br />
<img src="https://ccnav6.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/05/i274300v1n1_209630.jpg" /></p>
<ul>
<li>The woven copper braid should not have been removed.</li>
<li>The wrong type of connector is being used.</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>The untwisted length of each wire is too long.*</strong></span></li>
<li>The wires are too thick for the connector that is used.</li>
</ul>
<p><div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
When a cable to an RJ-45 connector is terminated, it is important to ensure that the untwisted wires are not too long and that the flexible plastic sheath surrounding the wires is crimped down and not the bare wires. None of the colored wires should be visible from the bottom of the jack.<br />
</p></div></li>
<li><strong>Which type of connector does a network interface card use?</strong>
<ul>
<li>DIN</li>
<li>PS-2</li>
<li>RJ-11</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>RJ-45*</strong></span></li>
</ul>
</li>
<li><strong>What is one advantage of using fiber optic cabling rather than copper cabling?</strong>
<ul>
<li>It is usually cheaper than copper cabling.</li>
<li>It is able to be installed around sharp bends.</li>
<li>It is easier to terminate and install than copper cabling.</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>It is able to carry signals much farther than copper cabling.*</strong></span></li>
</ul>
<p><div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
Copper cabling is usually cheaper and easier to install than fiber optic cabling. However, fiber cables generally have a much greater signaling range than copper.<br />
</p></div></li>
<li><strong>Why are two strands of fiber used for a single fiber optic connection?</strong>
<ul>
<li>The two strands allow the data to travel for longer distances without degrading.</li>
<li>They prevent crosstalk from causing interference on the connection.</li>
<li>They increase the speed at which the data can travel.</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>They allow for full-duplex connectivity.*</strong></span></li>
</ul>
<p><div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
Light can only travel in one direction down a single strand of fiber. In order to allow for full-duplex communication two strands of fiber must be connected between each device.<br />
</p></div></li>
<li><strong>A network administrator is designing the layout of a new wireless network. Which three areas of concern should be accounted for when building a wireless network? (Choose three.)</strong>
<ul>
<li>mobility options</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>security *</strong></span></li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>interference *</strong></span></li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>coverage area*</strong></span></li>
<li>extensive cabling</li>
<li>packet collision</li>
</ul>
<p><div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
The three areas of concern for wireless networks focus on the size of the coverage area, any nearby interference, and providing network security. Extensive cabling is not a concern for wireless networks, as a wireless network will require minimal cabling for providing wireless access to hosts. Mobility options are not a component of the areas of concern for wireless networks.<br />
</p></div></li>
<li><strong>Which layer of the OSI model is responsible for specifying the encapsulation method used for specific types of media?</strong>
<ul>
<li>application</li>
<li>transport</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>data link*</strong></span></li>
<li>physical</li>
</ul>
<p><div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
Encapsulation is a function of the data link layer. Different media types require different data link layer encapsulation.<br />
</p></div></li>
<li><strong>What are two services performed by the data link layer of the OSI model? (Choose two.)</strong>
<ul>
<li>It encrypts data packets.</li>
<li>It determines the path to forward packets.</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>It accepts Layer 3 packets and encapsulates them into frames. *</strong></span></li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>It provides media access control and performs error detection.*</strong></span></li>
<li>It monitors the Layer 2 communication by building a MAC address table.</li>
</ul>
<p><div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
The data link layer is responsible for the exchange of frames between nodes over a physical network media. Specifically the data link layer performs two basic services:<br />
It accepts Layer 3 packets and encapsulates them into frames.<br />
It provides media access control and performs error detection.<br />
Path determination is a service provided at Layer 3. A Layer 2 switch builds a MAC address table as part of its operation, but path determination is not the service that is provided by the data link layer.<br />
</p></div></li>
<li><strong>What is true concerning physical and logical topologies?</strong>
<ul>
<li>The logical topology is always the same as the physical topology.</li>
<li>Physical topologies are concerned with how a network transfers frames.</li>
<li>Physical topologies display the IP addressing scheme of each network.</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>Logical topologies refer to how a network transfers data between devices.*</strong></span></li>
</ul>
<p><div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
Physical topologies show the physical interconnection of devices. Logical topologies show the way the network will transfer data between connected nodes.<br />
</p></div></li>
<li><strong>Which method of data transfer allows information to be sent and received at the same time?</strong>
<ul>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong> full duplex*</strong></span></li>
<li>half duplex</li>
<li>multiplex</li>
<li>simplex</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li><strong>Which statement describes an extended star topology?</strong>
<ul>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>End devices connect to a central intermediate device, which in turn connects to other central intermediate devices.*</strong></span></li>
<li>End devices are connected together by a bus and each bus connects to a central intermediate device.</li>
<li>Each end system is connected to its respective neighbor via an intermediate device.</li>
<li>All end and intermediate devices are connected in a chain to each other.</li>
</ul>
<p><div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
In an extended star topology, central intermediate devices interconnect other star topologies.<br />
</p></div></li>
<li><strong>Refer to the exhibit. Which statement describes the media access control methods that are used by the networks in the exhibit?</strong><br />
<img src="https://ccnav6.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/05/i282597v1n1_208217.jpg" /></p>
<ul>
<li>All three networks use CSMA/CA</li>
<li>None of the networks require media access control.</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>Network 1 uses CSMA/CD and Network 3 uses CSMA/CA.*</strong></span></li>
<li>Network 1 uses CSMA/CA and Network 2 uses CSMA/CD.</li>
<li>Network 2 uses CSMA/CA and Network 3 uses CSMA/CD.</li>
</ul>
<p><div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
Network 1 represents an Ethernet LAN. Data on the wired LAN accesses the media using CSMA/CD. Network 2 represents a point-to-point WAN connection so no media access method is required. Network 3 represents a WLAN and data accesses the network using CSMA/CA.<br />
</p></div></li>
<li><strong>What is contained in the trailer of a data-link frame?</strong>
<ul>
<li>logical address</li>
<li>physical address</li>
<li>data</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>error detection*</strong></span></li>
</ul>
<p><div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
The trailer in a data-link frame contains error detection information that is pertinent to the frame included in the FCS field. The header contains control information, such as the addressing, while the area that is indicated by the word &#8220;data&#8221; includes the data, transport layer PDU, and the IP header.<br />
</p></div></li>
<li><strong>As data travels on the media in a stream of 1s and 0s how does a receiving node identify the beginning and end of a frame?</strong>
<ul>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>The transmitting node inserts start and stop bits into the frame.*</strong></span></li>
<li>The transmitting node sends a beacon to notify that a data frame is attached.</li>
<li>The receiving node identifies the beginning of a frame by seeing a physical address.</li>
<li>The transmitting node sends an out-of-band signal to the receiver about the beginning of the frame.</li>
</ul>
<p><div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
When data travels on the media, it is converted into a stream of 1s and 0s. The framing process inserts into the frame start and stop indicator flags so that the destination can detect the beginning and end of the frame.<br />
</p></div></li>
<li><strong>What is a role of the Logical Link Control sublayer?</strong>
<ul>
<li>to provide data link layer addressing</li>
<li>to provide access to various Layer 1 network technologies</li>
<li>to define the media access processes performed by network hardware</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>to mark frames to identify the network layer protocol being carried*</strong></span></li>
</ul>
<p><div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong>There are two data link sublayers, MAC and LLC. The LLC sublayer is responsible for communicating with the network layer and for tagging frames to identify what Layer 3 protocol is encapsulated.</p></div></li>
<li><strong>What is the definition of bandwidth?</strong>
<ul>
<li>the measure of usable data transferred over a given period of time</li>
<li>the speed at which bits travel on the network</li>
<li>the measure of the transfer of bits across the media over a given period of time</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>the amount of data that can flow from one place to another in a given amount of time*</strong></span></li>
</ul>
<p><div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong>Bandwidth is the measure of the capacity of a network medium to carry data. It is the amount of data that can move between two points on the network over a specific period of time, typically one second.</p></div></li>
<li><strong>What is the function of the CRC value that is found in the FCS field of a frame?</strong>
<ul>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>to verify the integrity of the received frame*</strong></span></li>
<li>to verify the physical address in the frame</li>
<li>to verify the logical address in the frame</li>
<li>to compute the checksum header for the data field in the frame</li>
</ul>
<p><div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
The CRC value in the FCS field of the received frame is compared to the computed CRC value of that frame, in order to verify the integrity of the frame. If the two values do not match, then the frame is discarded.<br />
</p></div></li>
<li><strong>Fill in the blank.</strong><br />
The term <span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>bandwidth </strong></span>indicates the capacity of a medium to carry data and it is typically measured in kilobits per second (kb/s) or megabits per second (Mb/s).<div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
Bandwidth is the capacity of a medium to carry data in a given amount of time. It is typically measured in kilobits per second (kb/s) or megabits per second (Mb/s).​<br />
</p></div></li>
<li><strong>Fill in the blank.</strong><br />
What acronym is used to reference the data link sublayer that identifies the network layer protocol encapsulated in the frame? <span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>LLC</strong></span><div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
Logical Link Control (LLC) is the data link sublayer that defines the software processes that provide services to the network layer protocols. LLC places information in the frame and that information identifies the network layer protocol that is encapsulated in the frame.<br />
</p></div></li>
<li><strong>Match the characteristics to the correct type of fiber. (Not all options are used.)</strong><img src="https://ccnav6.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/05/2017-05-22_164930.jpg" /><br />
<img src="https://ccnav6.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/05/2017-05-22_164930-1.jpg" /><strong>Place de options in the following order.</strong><br />
<strong>Multimode Fiber</strong><br />
<span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>LED as light source*</strong></span><br />
<span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>several paths of light into the fiber*</strong></span><br />
<span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>generally used with LANs*</strong></span><br />
<strong>Single-mode Fiber</strong><br />
<span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>only one ray of light into the fiber*</strong></span><br />
<span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>generally used for campus backbone*</strong></span><br />
<span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>laser as light source*</strong></span><br />
<div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
Single-mode fiber uses a laser as the light source. Its small core produces a single straight path for light and it is commonly used with campus backbones. Multimode fiber uses LEDs as the light source. Its larger core allows for multiple paths for the light. It is commonly used with LANs.<br />
</p></div></li>
<li><strong>Fill in the blank.</strong><br />
A physical topology that is a variation or combination of a point-to-point, hub and spoke, or mesh topology is commonly known as a <span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>hybrid</strong></span> topology.<br />
<div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
A hybrid topology is a variation or combination of a point-to-point, hub and spoke, or mesh topology. This may include a partial mesh or extended star topology.<br />
</p></div></li>
<li><strong>What are two examples of hybrid topologies? (Choose two.)</strong>
<ul>
<li>point-to-point</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>partial mesh*</strong></span></li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>extended star*</strong></span></li>
<li>hub and spoke</li>
<li>full mesh</li>
</ul>
<p><div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong>A hybrid topology is one that is a variation or a combination of other topologies. Both partial mesh and the extended star are examples of hybrid topologies.</p></div></li>
</ol>

<li><strong>Match the steps to the physical layer operations that occur when data is sent from one node and received at another node.</strong><br />
<img class="alignnone" src="https://ccnav6.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/02/p23-exa4-ccna1.png" alt="" width="734" height="574" /><br />

Network 2 uses CSMA/CA and Network 3 uses CSMA/CD.</li>

<!-- 5 chapter -->

<li><strong>What happens to runt frames received by a Cisco Ethernet switch?</strong>
<ul>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>The frame is dropped.*</strong></span></li>
<li>The frame is returned to the originating network device.</li>
<li>The frame is broadcast to all other devices on the same network.</li>
<li>The frame is sent to the default gateway.</li>
</ul>
<p><div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
In an attempt to conserve bandwidth and not forward useless frames, Ethernet devices drop frames that are considered to be runt (less than 64 bytes) or jumbo (greater than 1500 bytes) frames.<br />
</p></div></li>
<p></p>
<li><strong>What are the two sizes (minimum and maximum) of an Ethernet frame? (Choose two.)</strong>
<ul>
<li>56 bytes</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>64 bytes*</strong></span></li>
<li>128 bytes</li>
<li>1024 bytes</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>1518 bytes*</strong></span></li>
</ul>
<p><div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
The minimum Ethernet frame is 64 bytes. The maximum Ethernet frame is 1518 bytes. A network technician must know the minimum and maximum frame size in order to recognize runt and jumbo frames.<br />
</p></div></li>
<p></p>
<li><strong>What statement describes Ethernet?</strong>
<ul>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>It defines the most common LAN type in the world.*</strong></span></li>
<li>It is the required Layer 1 and 2 standard for Internet communication.</li>
<li>It defines a standard model used to describe how networking works.</li>
<li>It connects multiple sites such as routers located in different countries.</li>
</ul>
<p><div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
Ethernet is the most common LAN protocol in the world. It operates at Layer 1 and 2, but is not required for Internet communication. The OSI model is used to describe how networks operate. A WAN connects multiple sites located in different countries.<br />
</p></div></li>
<p></p>
<li><strong>Which two statements describe features or functions of the logical link control sublayer in Ethernet standards? (Choose two.)</strong>
<ul>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong> Logical link control is implemented in software.*</strong></span></li>
<li>Logical link control is specified in the IEEE 802.3 standard.</li>
<li>The LLC sublayer adds a header and a trailer to the data.</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>The data link layer uses LLC to communicate with the upper layers of the protocol suite.*</strong></span></li>
<li>The LLC sublayer is responsible for the placement and retrieval of frames on and off the media.</li>
</ul>
<p><div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
Logical link control is implemented in software and enables the data link layer to communicate with the upper layers of the protocol suite. Logical link control is specified in the IEEE 802.2 standard. IEEE 802.3 is a suite of standards that define the different Ethernet types. The MAC (Media Access Control) sublayer is responsible for the placement and retrieval of frames on and off the media. The MAC sublayer is also responsible for adding a header and a trailer to the network layer protocol data unit (PDU).<br />
</p></div></li>
<p></p>
<li><strong>What statement describes a characteristic of MAC addresses?</strong>
<ul>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>They must be globally unique.*</strong></span></li>
<li>They are only routable within the private network.</li>
<li>They are added as part of a Layer 3 PDU.</li>
<li>They have a 32-bit binary value.</li>
</ul>
<p><div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
Any vendor selling Ethernet devices must register with the IEEE to ensure the vendor is assigned a unique 24-bit code, which becomes the first 24 bits of the MAC address. The last 24 bits of the MAC address are generated per hardware device. This helps to ensure globally unique addresses for each Ethernet device.<br />
</p></div></li>
<p></p>
<li><strong>Which statement is true about MAC addresses?</strong>
<ul>
<li>MAC addresses are implemented by software.</li>
<li>A NIC only needs a MAC address if connected to a WAN.</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>The first three bytes are used by the vendor assigned OUI.*</strong></span></li>
<li>The ISO is responsible for MAC addresses regulations.</li>
</ul>
<p><div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
A MAC address is composed of 6 bytes. The first 3 bytes are used for vendor identification and the last 3 bytes must be assigned a unique value within the same OUI. MAC addresses are implemented in hardware. A NIC needs a MAC address to communicate over the LAN. The IEEE regulates the MAC addresses.<br />
</p></div></li>
<p></p>
<li><strong>Which destination address is used in an ARP request frame?</strong>
<ul>
<li>0.0.0.0</li>
<li>255.255.255.255</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>FFFF.FFFF.FFFF*</strong></span></li>
<li>127.0.0.1</li>
<li>01-00-5E-00-AA-23</li>
</ul>
<p><div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
The purpose of an ARP request is to find the MAC address of the destination host on an Ethernet LAN. The ARP process sends a Layer 2 broadcast to all devices on the Ethernet LAN. The frame contains the IP address of the destination and the broadcast MAC address, FFFF.FFFF.FFFF.<br />
</p></div></li>
<p></p>
<li><strong>What addressing information is recorded by a switch to build its MAC address table?</strong>
<ul>
<li>the destination Layer 3 address of incoming packets</li>
<li>the destination Layer 2 address of outgoing frames</li>
<li>the source Layer 3 address of outgoing packets</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>the source Layer 2 address of incoming frames*</strong></span></li>
</ul>
<p><div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
A switch builds a MAC address table by inspecting incoming Layer 2 frames and recording the source MAC address found in the frame header. The discovered and recorded MAC address is then associated with the port used to receive the frame.<br />
</p></div></li>
<p></p>
<li><strong>Refer to the exhibit. The exhibit shows a small switched network and the contents of the MAC address table of the switch. PC1 has sent a frame addressed to PC3. What will the switch do with the frame?</strong><br />
<img src="https://ccnav6.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/05/i275394v1n1_207267.jpg" /></p>
<ul>
<li>The switch will discard the frame.</li>
<li>The switch will forward the frame only to port 2.</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>The switch will forward the frame to all ports except port 4.*</strong></span></li>
<li>The switch will forward the frame to all ports.</li>
<li>The switch will forward the frame only to ports 1 and 3.</li>
</ul>
<p><div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
The MAC address of PC3 is not present in the MAC table of the switch. Because the switch does not know where to send the frame that is addressed to PC3, it will forward the frame to all the switch ports, except for port 4, which is the incoming port.<br />
</p></div></li>
<p></p>
<li><strong>Which switching method uses the CRC value in a frame?</strong>
<ul>
<li>cut-through</li>
<li>fast-forward</li>
<li>fragment-free</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>store-and-forward*</strong></span></li>
</ul>
<p><div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
When the store-and-forward switching method is used, the switch receives the complete frame before forwarding it on to the destination. The cyclic redundancy check (CRC) part of the trailer is used to determine if the frame has been modified during transit.​​ In contrast, a cut-through switch forwards the frame once the destination Layer 2 address is read. Two types of cut-through switching methods are fast-forward and fragment-free.<br />
</p></div></li>
<p></p>
<li><strong>What is auto-MDIX?</strong>
<ul>
<li>a type of Cisco switch</li>
<li>an Ethernet connector type</li>
<li>a type of port on a Cisco switch</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>a feature that detects Ethernet cable type*</strong></span></li>
</ul>
<p><div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
Auto-MDIX is a feature that is enabled on the latest Cisco switches and that allows the switch to detect and use whatever type of cable is attached to a specific port.​​<br />
</p></div></li>
<p></p>
<li><strong>Refer to the exhibit. PC1 issues an ARP request because it needs to send a packet to PC2. In this scenario, what will happen next?</strong><br />
<img src="https://ccnav6.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/05/i209824v1n1_209824.jpg" /></p>
<ul>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong> PC2 will send an ARP reply with its MAC address.*</strong></span></li>
<li>RT1 will send an ARP reply with its Fa0/0 MAC address.</li>
<li>RT1 will send an ARP reply with the PC2 MAC address.</li>
<li>SW1 will send an ARP reply with the PC2 MAC address.</li>
<li>SW1 will send an ARP reply with its Fa0/1 MAC address.</li>
</ul>
<p><div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
When a network device wants to communicate with another device on the same network, it sends a broadcast ARP request. In this case, the request will contain the IP address of PC2. The destination device (PC2) sends an ARP reply with its MAC address.<br />
</p></div></li>
<p></p>
<li><strong>What is the aim of an ARP spoofing attack?</strong>
<ul>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>to associate IP addresses to the wrong MAC address*</strong></span></li>
<li>to overwhelm network hosts with ARP requests</li>
<li>to flood the network with ARP reply broadcasts</li>
<li>to fill switch MAC address tables with bogus addresses</li>
</ul>
</li>
<p></p>
<li><strong>What is a characteristic of port-based memory buffering?</strong>
<ul>
<li>Frames in the memory buffer are dynamically linked to destination ports.</li>
<li>All frames are stored in a common memory buffer.</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>Frames are buffered in queues linked to specific ports.*</strong></span></li>
<li>All ports on a switch share a single memory buffer.</li>
</ul>
<p><div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong>Buffering is a technique used by Ethernet switches to store frames until they can be transmitted. With port-based buffering, frames are stored in queues that are linked to specific incoming and outgoing ports.</p></div></li>
<p></p>
<li><strong>What is the minimum Ethernet frame size that will not be discarded by the receiver as a runt frame?</strong>
<ul>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>64 bytes*</strong></span></li>
<li>512 bytes</li>
<li>1024 bytes</li>
<li>1500 bytes</li>
</ul>
</li>
<p></p>
<li><strong>What are two potential network problems that can result from ARP operation? (Choose two.)</strong>
<ul>
<li>Manually configuring static ARP associations could facilitate ARP poisoning or MAC address spoofing.</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>On large networks with low bandwidth, multiple ARP broadcasts could cause data communication delays. *</strong></span></li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>Network attackers could manipulate MAC address and IP address mappings in ARP messages with the intent of intercepting network traffic.*</strong></span></li>
<li>Large numbers of ARP request broadcasts could cause the host MAC address table to overflow and prevent the host from communicating on the network.</li>
<li>Multiple ARP replies result in the switch MAC address table containing entries that match the MAC addresses of hosts that are connected to the relevant switch port.</li>
</ul>
<p><div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
Large numbers of ARP broadcast messages could cause momentary data communications delays. Network attackers could manipulate MAC address and IP address mappings in ARP messages with the intent to intercept network traffic. ARP requests and replies cause entries to be made into the ARP table, not the MAC address table. ARP table overflows are very unlikely. Manually configuring static ARP associations is a way to prevent, not facilitate, ARP poisoning and MAC address spoofing. Multiple ARP replies resulting in the switch MAC address table containing entries that match the MAC addresses of connected nodes and are associated with the relevant switch port are required for normal switch frame forwarding operations. It is not an ARP caused network problem.<br />
</p></div></li>
<p></p>
<li><strong>Fill in the blank.</strong><br />
A collision fragment, also known as a <span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>RUNT </strong></span>frame, is a frame of fewer than 64 bytes in length.<div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
A runt frame is a frame of fewer than 64 bytes, usually generated by a collision or a network interface failure.<br />
</p></div></li>
<p></p>
<li><strong>Fill in the blank.</strong><br />
On a Cisco switch, <span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>port-based</strong></span> memory buffering is used to buffer frames in queues linked to specific incoming and outgoing ports.</li>
<li><strong>Fill in the blank.</strong><br />
ARP <span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>spoofing</strong></span> is a technique that is used to send fake ARP messages to other hosts in the LAN. The aim is to associate IP addresses to the wrong MAC addresses.<div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
ARP spoofing or ARP poisoning is a technique used by an attacker to reply to an ARP request for an IPv4 address belonging to another device, such as the default gateway.<br />
</p></div></li>
<p></p>
<li><strong>Which statement describes the treatment of ARP requests on the local link?</strong><br />
They must be forwarded by all routers on the local network.<br />
<span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>They are received and processed by every device on the local network.*</strong></span><br />
They are dropped by all switches on the local network.<br />
They are received and processed only by the target device.</li>
<li><strong>Refer to the exhibit. </strong><br />
<img src="https://ccnav6.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/05/i275353v1n1_275353.jpg" /><br />
<strong>The switches are in their default configuration. Host A needs to communicate with host D, but host A does not have the MAC address for its default gateway. Which network hosts will receive the ARP request sent by host A?</strong><br />
only host D<br />
only router R1<br />
only hosts A, B, and C<br />
only hosts A, B, C, and D<br />
only hosts B and C<br />
<span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>only hosts B, C, and router R1*</strong></span><div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
Since host A does not have the MAC address of the default gateway in its ARP table, host A sends an ARP broadcast. The ARP broadcast would be sent to every device on the local network. Hosts B, C, and router R1 would receive the broadcast. Router R1 would not forward the message.<br />
</p></div></li>
<p></p>
<li><strong>Refer to the exhibit.</strong><br />
<img src="https://ccnav6.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/05/i274591v1n1_274591.jpg" /><br />
<strong>A switch with a default configuration connects four hosts. The ARP table for host A is shown. What happens when host A wants to send an IP packet to host D?</strong>Host A sends an ARP request to the MAC address of host D.<br />
Host D sends an ARP request to host A.<br />
Host A sends out the packet to the switch. The switch sends the packet only to the host D, which in turn responds.<br />
<span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>Host A sends out a broadcast of FF:FF:FF:FF:FF:FF. Every other host connected to the switch receives the broadcast and host D responds with its MAC address.*</strong></span><div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
Whenever the destination MAC address is not contained within the ARP table of the originating host, the host (host A in this example) will send a Layer 2 broadcast that has a destination MAC address of FF:FF:FF:FF:FF:FF. All devices on the same network receive this broadcast. Host D will respond to this broadcast.<br />
</p></div></li>
<p></p>
<li><strong>True or False?</strong><br />
<strong>When a device is sending data to another device on a remote network, the Ethernet frame is sent to the MAC address of the default gateway.</strong><br />
<span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>true*</strong></span><br />
false<div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
A MAC address is only useful on the local Ethernet network. When data is destined for a remote network of any type, the data is sent to the default gateway device, the Layer 3 device that routes for the local network.<br />
</p></div></li>
<p></p>
<li><strong>The ARP table in a switch maps which two types of address together?</strong><br />
<span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>Layer 3 address to a Layer 2 address*</strong></span><br />
Layer 3 address to a Layer 4 address<br />
Layer 4 address to a Layer 2 address<br />
Layer 2 address to a Layer 4 address<div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
The switch ARP table keeps a mapping of Layer 2 MAC addresses to Layer 3 IP addresses. These mappings can be learned by the switch dynamically through ARP or statically through manual configuration.<br />
</p></div></li>
<p></p>
<li><strong>Match the characteristic to the forwarding method. (Not all options are used.)</strong><img src="https://ccnav6.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/05/2017-05-22_175719.jpg" /><img src="https://ccnav6.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/05/2017-05-22_175719-1.jpg" /><strong>Sort elements</strong><br />
<strong>cut-through (A) -&gt; <span style="color: #ff0000;">low latency (A)*</span></strong><br />
<strong>cut-through (B) -&gt; <span style="color: #ff0000;">may forward runt frames (B)*</span></strong><br />
<strong>cut-through (C) -&gt; <span style="color: #ff0000;">begins forwarding when the destination address is received (C)*</span></strong><br />
<strong>store-and-forward (D) -&gt; <span style="color: #ff0000;">always stores the entire frame (D)*</span></strong><br />
<strong>store-and-forward (E) -&gt; <span style="color: #ff0000;">checks the CRC before forwarding (E)*</span></strong><br />
<strong>store-and-forward (F) -&gt; <span style="color: #ff0000;">checks the frame length before forwarding (F)</span></strong><div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
A store-and-forward switch always stores the entire frame before forwarding, and checks its CRC and frame length. A cut-through switch can forward frames before receiving the destination address field, thus presenting less latency than a store-and-forward switch. Because the frame can begin to be forwarded before it is completely received, the switch may transmit a corrupt or runt frame. All forwarding methods require a Layer 2 switch to forward broadcast frames.<br />
</p></div></li>
<p>
</ol>
<h2>Other Questions</h2>
<ol>
<li><strong>What is a characteristic of a contention-based access method?</strong>
<ul>
<li>It processes more overhead than the controlled access methods do.</li>
<li>It has mechanisms to track the turns to access the media.</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>It is a nondeterministic method.*</strong></span></li>
<li>It scales very well under heavy media use.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<p></p>
<li><strong>What is the purpose of the preamble in an Ethernet frame?</strong>
<ul>
<li>is used as a padding for data</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>is used for timing synchronization*</strong></span></li>
<li>is used to identify the source address</li>
<li>is used to identify the destination address</li>
</ul>
</li>
<p></p>
<li><strong>What is the Layer 2 multicast MAC address that corresponds to the Layer 3 IPv4 multicast address 224.139.34.56?</strong>
<ul>
<li>00-00-00-0B-22-38</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>01-00-5E-0B-22-38*</strong></span></li>
<li>01-5E-00-0B-22-38</li>
<li>FE-80-00-0B-22-38</li>
<li>FF-FF-FF-0B-22-38</li>
</ul>
</li>
<p></p>
<li><strong>Which two statements are correct about MAC and IP addresses during data transmission if NAT is not involved? (Choose two.)</strong>
<ul>
<li>A packet that has crossed four routers has changed the destination IP address four times.</li>
<li>Destination MAC addresses will never change in a frame that goes across seven routers.</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>Destination and source MAC addresses have local significance and change every time a frame goes from one LAN to another. *</strong></span></li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>Destination IP addresses in a packet header remain constant along the entire path to a target host.*</strong></span></li>
<li>Every time a frame is encapsulated with a new destination MAC address, a new destination IP address is needed.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<p></p>
<li><strong>What are two features of ARP? (Choose two.)</strong>
<ul>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>If a host is ready to send a packet to a local destination device and it has the IP address but not the MAC address of the destination, it generates an ARP broadcast.*</strong></span></li>
<li>An ARP request is sent to all devices on the Ethernet LAN and contains the IP address of the destination host and its multicast MAC address.</li>
<li>When a host is encapsulating a packet into a frame, it refers to the MAC address table to determine the mapping of IP addresses to MAC addresses.</li>
<li>If no device responds to the ARP request, then the originating node will broadcast the data packet to all devices on the network segment.</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>If a device receiving an ARP request has the destination IPv4 address, it responds with an ARP reply.*</strong></span></li>
</ul>
</li>
<p></p>
<li><strong>A host is trying to send a packet to a device on a remote LAN segment, but there are currently no mappings in its ARP cache. How will the device obtain a destination MAC address?</strong>
<ul>
<li>It will send an ARP request for the MAC address of the destination device.</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>It will send an ARP request for the MAC address of the default gateway. *</strong></span></li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong><span style="color: #000000;">It will send the frame and use its own MAC address as the destination.</span> *</strong></span></li>
<li>It will send the frame with a broadcast MAC address.</li>
<li>It will send a request to the DNS server for the destination MAC address.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<li><strong>A network administrator issues the following commands on a Layer 3 switch:</strong>
<pre>
DLS1(config)# interface f0/3
DLS1(config-if)# no switchport
DLS1(config-if)# ip address 172.16.0.1 255.255.255.0
DLS1(config-if)# no shutdown
DLS1(config-if)# end
</pre>
<p><strong>What is the administrator configuring?</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>a Cisco Express Forwarding instance</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>a routed port*</strong></span></li>
<li>a trunk interface</li>
<li>a switched virtual interface</li>
</ul>
</li>
<p></p>
<li><strong>The binary number 0000 1010 can be expressed as “<span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>A</strong></span>” in hexadecimal.<br />
Match the seven fields of an Ethernet frame to their respective contents. (Not all options are used.)</strong><br />
<img class="alignnone" src="https://ccnav6.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/02/p23-exa5-ccna1.png" alt="" width="624" height="574" /><br />
<strong>Sort elements</strong><br />
<strong>Start Frame Delimiter -&gt; <span style="color: #ff0000;">Field 2*</span></strong><br />
<strong>Source MAC Address -&gt; <span style="color: #ff0000;">Field 4*</span></strong><br />
<strong>Encapsulated Data -&gt; <span style="color: #ff0000;">Field 6*</span></strong><br />
<strong>Preamble -&gt; <span style="color: #ff0000;">Beginning of frame – Field 1*</span></strong><br />
<strong>Destination MAC Address -&gt; <span style="color: #ff0000;">Field 3*</span></strong><br />
<strong>Length/Type -&gt; <span style="color: #ff0000;">Field 5*</span></strong><br />
<strong>Frame Check Sequence -&gt; <span style="color: #ff0000;">End of frame – Field 7</span></strong>
</li>

<!-- 6 chapter -->

<li>the de-encapsulation of headers from lower layers</li>
<li>the selection of paths for and direct packets toward the destination</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>the ability to operate without regard to the data that is carried in each packet*</strong></span></li>
<li>the ability to manage the data transport between processes running on hosts</li>
</ul>
</li>
<p>
<div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
The function of the network layer protocols specifies the packet structure and processing used to carry the data from one host to another host. The actual communication data is encapsulated in the network layer PDU. The feature of its operation without regard to the data carried in each packet allows the network layer to carry packets for multiple types of communications.<br />
</p></div></li>
<p></p>
<li style="text-align: justify;"><strong>What are two characteristics of IP? (Choose two.)</strong>
<ul>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>does not require a dedicated end-to-end connection *</strong></span></li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>operates independently of the network media*</strong></span></li>
<li>retransmits packets if errors occur</li>
<li>re-assembles out of order packets into the correct order at the receiver end</li>
<li>guarantees delivery of packets</li>
</ul>
</li>
<p>
<div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
The Internet Protocol (IP) is a connectionless, best effort protocol. This means that IP requires no end-to-end connection nor does it guarantee delivery of packets. IP is also media independent, which means it operates independently of the network media carrying the packets.<br />
</p></div></li>
<p></p>
<li style="text-align: justify;"><strong>When a connectionless protocol is in use at a lower layer of the OSI model, how is missing data detected and retransmitted if necessary?</strong>
<ul>
<li>Connectionless acknowledgements are used to request retransmission.</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>Upper-layer connection-oriented protocols keep track of the data received and can request retransmission from the upper-level protocols on the sending host.*</strong></span></li>
<li>Network layer IP protocols manage the communication sessions if connection-oriented transport services are not available.</li>
<li>The best-effort delivery process guarantees that all packets that are sent are received.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<p>
<div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
When connectionless protocols are in use at a lower layer of the OSI model, upper-level protocols may need to work together on the sending and receiving hosts to account for and retransmit lost data. In some cases, this is not necessary, because for some applications a certain amount of data loss is tolerable.<br />
</p></div></li>
<p></p>
<li style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Which field in the IPv4 header is used to prevent a packet from traversing a network endlessly?</strong>
<ul>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>Time-to-Live*</strong></span></li>
<li>Sequence Number</li>
<li>Acknowledgment Number</li>
<li>Differentiated Services</li>
</ul>
</li>
<p>
<div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
The value of the Time-to-Live (TTL) field in the IPv4 header is used to limit the lifetime of a packet. The sending host sets the initial TTL value; which is decreased by one each time the packet is processed by a router. If the TTL field decrements to zero, the router discards the packet and sends an Internet Control Message Protocol (ICMP) Time Exceeded message to the source IP address. The Differentiated Services (DS) field is used to determine the priority of each packet. Sequence Number and Acknowledgment Number are two fields in the TCP header.<br />
</p></div></li>
<p></p>
<li style="text-align: justify;"><strong>What IPv4 header field identifies the upper layer protocol carried in the packet?</strong>
<ul>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>Protocol*</strong></span></li>
<li>Identification</li>
<li>Version</li>
<li>Differentiated Services</li>
</ul>
</li>
<p>
<div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
It is the Protocol field in the IP header that identifies the upper-layer protocol the packet is carrying. The Version field identifies the IP version. The Differential Services field is used for setting packet priority. The Identification field is used to reorder fragmented packets.<br />
</p></div></li>
<p></p>
<li style="text-align: justify;"><strong>What is one advantage that the IPv6 simplified header offers over IPv4?</strong>
<ul>
<li>smaller-sized header</li>
<li>little requirement for processing checksums</li>
<li>smaller-sized source and destination IP addresses</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>efficient packet handling*</strong></span></li>
</ul>
</li>
<p>
<div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
The IPv6 simplified header offers several advantages over IPv4:<br />
· Better routing efficiency and efficient packet handling for performance and forwarding-rate scalability<br />
· No requirement for processing checksums<br />
· Simplified and more efficient extension header mechanisms (as opposed to the IPv4 Options field)<br />
· A Flow Label field for per-flow processing with no need to open the transport inner packet to identify the various traffic flows<br />
</p></div></li>
<p></p>
<li style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Refer to the exhibit. Which route from the PC1 routing table will be used to reach PC2?</strong><br />
<img src="https://ccnav6.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/05/i275479v1n1_206386.jpg" /></p>
<p>A. <img src="https://ccnav6.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/05/aaa.jpg" /></p>
<p>B. <img src="https://ccnav6.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/05/bbb.jpg" /></p>
<p>C. <img src="https://ccnav6.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/05/ccc.jpg" /></p>
<p>D. <img src="https://ccnav6.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/05/ddd.jpg" /></p>
<p><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>Correct answer: A</strong></span></p>
<p><div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
PC1 and PC2 are both on network 192.168.10.0 with mask 255.255.255.0, so there is no need to access the default gateway (entry 0.0.0.0 0.0.0.0). Entry 127.0.0.1 255.255.255.255 is the loopback interface and entry 192.168.10.10 255.255.255.255 identifies the PC1 address interface.<br />
</p></div></li>
<p></p>
<li style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Refer to the exhibit. R1 receives a packet destined for the IP address 192.168.2.10. Out which interface will R1 forward the packet?</strong><br />
<img src="https://ccnav6.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/05/i206421v1n1_Question3.png" /></p>
<ul>
<li>FastEthernet0/0</li>
<li>FastEthernet0/1</li>
<li>Serial0/0/0</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>Serial0/0/1*</strong></span></li>
</ul>
</li>
<p>
<div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
If a route in the routing table points to a next hop address, the router will perform a second lookup to determine out which interface the next hop is located.<br />
</p></div></li>
<p></p>
<li style="text-align: justify;"><strong>What type of route is indicated by the code C in an IPv4 routing table on a Cisco router?</strong>
<ul>
<li>static route</li>
<li>default route</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>directly connected route*</strong></span></li>
<li>dynamic route that is learned through EIGRP</li>
</ul>
</li>
<p>
<div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
Some of the IPv4 routing table codes include the following:<br />
C – directly connected<br />
S – static<br />
D – EIGRP<br />
* &#8211; candidate default<br />
</p></div></li>
<p></p>
<li style="text-align: justify;"><strong>What routing table entry has a next hop address associated with a destination network?</strong>
<ul>
<li>directly-connected routes</li>
<li>local routes</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>remote routes*</strong></span></li>
<li>C and L source routes</li>
</ul>
</li>
<p>
<div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
Routing table entries for remote routes will have a next hop IP address. The next hop IP address is the address of the router interface of the next device to be used to reach the destination network. Directly-connected and local routes have no next hop, because they do not require going through another router to be reached.<br />
</p></div></li>
<p></p>
<li style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Which statement describes a hardware feature of a Cisco 1941 router that has the default hardware configuration?</strong>
<ul>
<li>It does not have an AUX port.</li>
<li>It has three FastEthernet interfaces for LAN access.</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>It has two types of ports that can be used to access the console.*</strong></span></li>
<li>It does not require a CPU because it relies on Compact Flash to run the IOS.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<p>
<div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
The connections in a Cisco 1941 router include two types of ports that are used for initial configuration and command-line interface management access. The two ports are the regular RJ-45 port and a new USB Type-B (mini-B USB) connector. In addition, the router has an AUX port for remote management access, and two Gigabit Ethernet interfaces for LAN access. Compact Flash can be used increase device storage, but it does not perform the functions of the CPU, which is required for operation of the device.<br />
</p></div></li>
<p></p>
<li style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Following default settings, what is the next step in the router boot sequence after the IOS loads from flash?</strong>
<ul>
<li>Perform the POST routine.</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>Locate and load the startup-config file from NVRAM.*</strong></span></li>
<li>Load the bootstrap program from ROM.</li>
<li>Load the running-config file from RAM.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<p>
<div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
There are three major steps to the router boot sequence:<br />
Perform Power-On-Self-Test (POST)<br />
Load the IOS from Flash or TFTP server<br />
Load the startup configuration file from NVRAM<br />
</p></div></li>
<p></p>
<li style="text-align: justify;"><strong>What are two types of router interfaces? (Choose two.)</strong>
<ul>
<li>SVI</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>LAN*</strong></span></li>
<li>DHCP</li>
<li>Telnet</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>WAN*</strong></span></li>
</ul>
</li>
<p>
<div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
Router interfaces can be grouped into two categories:<br />
· LAN interfaces &#8211; Used for connecting cables that terminate with LAN devices, such as computers and switches. This interface can also be used to connect routers to each other.<br />
· WAN interfaces &#8211; Used for connecting routers to external networks, usually over a larger geographical distance.<br />
</p></div></li>
<p></p>
<li style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Which two pieces of information are in the RAM of a Cisco router during normal operation? (Choose two.)</strong>
<ul>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>Cisco IOS*</strong></span></li>
<li>backup IOS file</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>IP routing table*</strong></span></li>
<li>basic diagnostic software</li>
<li>startup configuration file</li>
</ul>
</li>
<p>
<div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
The Cisco IOS file is stored in flash memory and copied into RAM during the boot up. The IP routing table is also stored in RAM. The basic diagnostic software is stored in ROM and the startup configuration file is stored in NVRAM.<br />
</p></div></li>
<p></p>
<li style="text-align: justify;"><strong><strong>A router boots and enters setup mode. What is the reason for this?</strong></strong>
<ul>
<li>The IOS image is corrupt.</li>
<li>Cisco IOS is missing from flash memory.</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>The configuration file is missing from NVRAM.*</strong></span></li>
<li>The POST process has detected hardware failure.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<p></p>
<li style="text-align: justify;"><strong>What is the purpose of the startup configuration file on a Cisco router?</strong>
<ul>
<li>to facilitate the basic operation of the hardware components of a device</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>to contain the commands that are used to initially configure a router on startup*</strong></span></li>
<li>to contain the configuration commands that the router IOS is currently using</li>
<li>to provide a limited backup version of the IOS, in case the router cannot load the full featured IOS</li>
</ul>
</li>
<p>
<div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
The startup configuration file is stored in NVRAM and contains the commands needed to initially configure a router. It also creates the running configuration file that is stored in in RAM.<br />
</p></div></li>
<p></p>
<li style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Which three commands are used to set up secure access to a router through a connection to the console interface? (Choose three.)</strong>
<ul>
<li>interface fastethernet 0/0</li>
<li>line vty 0 4</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>line console 0*</strong></span></li>
<li>enable secret cisco</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>login *</strong></span></li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>password cisco *</strong></span></li>
</ul>
</li>
<p>
<div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
The three commands needed to password protect the console port are as follows:<br />
line console 0<br />
password cisco<br />
login<br />
Theinterface fastethernet 0/0 command is commonly used to access the configuration mode used to apply specific parameters such as the IP address to the Fa0/0 port. The line vty 0 4 command is used to access the configuration mode for Telnet. The0and 4 parameters specify ports 0 through 4, or a maximum of five simultaneous Telnet connections. The enable secret command is used to apply a password used on the router to access the privileged mode.<br />
</p></div></li>
<p></p>
<li style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Which characteristic describes an IPv6 enhancement over IPv4?</strong>
<ul>
<li>IPv6 addresses are based on 128-bit flat addressing as opposed to IPv4 which is based on 32-bit hierarchical addressing.</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>The IPv6 header is simpler than the IPv4 header is, which improves packet handling.*</strong></span></li>
<li>Both IPv4 and IPv6 support authentication, but only IPv6 supports privacy capabilities.</li>
<li>The IPv6 address space is four times bigger than the IPv4 address space.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<p>
<div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
IPv6 addresses are based on 128-bit hierarchical addressing, and the IPv6 header has been simplified with fewer fields, improving packet handling. IPv6 natively supports authentication and privacy capabilities as opposed to IPv4 that needs additional features to support those. The IPv6 address space is many times bigger than IPv4 address space.<br />
</p></div></li>
<p></p>
<li style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Open the PT Activity. The enable password on all devices is cisco.<br />
Perform the tasks in the activity instructions and then answer the question.</strong><br />
<strong>For what reason is the failure occurring?</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>PC1 has an incorrect default gateway configured.</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>SW1 does not have a default gateway configured.*</strong></span></li>
<li>The IP address of SW1 is configured in a wrong subnet.</li>
<li>PC2 has an incorrect default gateway configured.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<p>
<div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
The ip default-gateway command is missing on the SW1 configuration. Packets from PC2 are able to successfully reach SW1, but SW1 is unable to forward reply packets beyond the local network without the ip default-gateway command issued.<br />
</p></div></li>
<p></p>
<li><strong>Match the command with the device mode at which the command is entered. (Not all options are used.)</strong>
<ul>
<li style="text-align: justify;">Question<br />
<img src="https://ccnav6.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/05/2017-05-23_115945.png" /></li>
<li>Answer<br />
<img src="https://ccnav6.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/05/2017-05-23_115945-1.png" /></li>
</ul>
</li>
<p>
<div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
The enable command is entered in R1&gt; mode. The login command is entered in R1(config-line)# mode. The copy running-config startup-config command is entered in R1# mode. The ip address 192.168.4.4 255.255.255.0 command is entered in R1(config-if)# mode. The service password-encryption command is entered in global configuration mode.<br />
</p></div></li>

<h2>Other Questions</h2>
<li><strong>When connectionless protocols are implemented at the lower layers of the OSI model, what are usually used to acknowledge the data receipt and request the retransmission of missing data?</strong>
<ul>
<li>connectionless acknowledgements</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>upper-layer connection-oriented protocols*</strong></span></li>
<li>Network layer IP protocols</li>
<li>Transport layer UDP protocols</li>
</ul>
</li>
<p></p>
<li><strong>Which IPv4 header field is responsible for defining the priority of the packet?</strong>
<ul>
<li>flow label</li>
<li>flags</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>differentiated services*</strong></span></li>
<li>traffic class</li>
</ul>
</li>
<p></p>
<li><strong>Why is NAT not needed in IPv6?</strong>
<ul>
<li>Because IPv6 has integrated security, there is no need to hide the IPv6 addresses of internal networks.?</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>Any host or user can get a public IPv6 network address because the number of available IPv6 addresses is extremely large.?*</strong></span></li>
<li>The problems that are induced by NAT applications are solved because the IPv6 header improves packet handling by intermediate routers.?</li>
<li>The end-to-end connectivity problems that are caused by NAT are solved because the number of routes increases with the number of nodes that are connected to the Internet.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<p></p>
<li><strong>What is a service provided by the Flow Label field of the IPv6 header?</strong>
<ul>
<li>It limits the lifetime of a packet.</li>
<li>It identifies the total length of the IPv6 packet.</li>
<li>It classifies packets for traffic congestion control.</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>It informs network devices to maintain the same path for real-time application packets.*</strong></span></li>
</ul>
</li>
<p></p>
<li><strong>How do hosts ensure that their packets are directed to the correct network destination?</strong>
<ul>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>They have to keep their own local routing table that contains a route to the loopback interface, a local network route, and a remote default route.?*</strong></span></li>
<li>They always direct their packets to the default gateway, which will be responsible for the packet delivery.</li>
<li>They search in their own local routing table for a route to the network destination address and pass this information to the default gateway.</li>
<li>They send a query packet to the default gateway asking for the best route.</li>
</ul>
</li>

<ul>
<li>discard the traffic after consulting the route table</li>
<li>look up the next-hop address for the packet</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>switch the packet to the directly connected interface*</strong></span></li>
<li>analyze the destination IP address</li>
</ul>
</li>

<li><strong>A technician is manually configuring a computer with the necessary IP parameters to communicate over the corporate network. The computer already has an IP address, a subnet mask, and a DNS server. What else has to be configured for Internet access?</strong>
<ul>
<li>the WINS server address</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>the default gateway address*</strong></span></li>
<li>the MAC address</li>
<li>the domain name of the organization</li>
</ul>
</li>
<p></p>
<li><strong>A computer has to send a packet to a destination host in the same LAN. How will the packet be sent?</strong>
<ul>
<li>The packet will be sent to the default gateway first, and then, depending on the response from the gateway, it may be sent to the destination host.</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>The packet will be sent directly to the destination host.*</strong></span></li>
<li>The packet will first be sent to the default gateway, and then from the default gateway it will be sent directly to the destination host.</li>
<li>The packet will be sent only to the default gateway.</li>
</ul>
</li>
