<li><strong>A newly hired network technician is given the task of ordering new hardware for a small business with a large growth forecast. Which primary factor should the technician be concerned with when choosing the new devices?</strong>
<ul>
<li>devices with a fixed number and type of interfaces</li>
<li>devices that have support for network monitoring</li>
<li>redundant devices</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>devices with support for modularity*</strong></span></li>
</ul>
<p><div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
In a small business with a large growth forecast, the primary influencing factor would be the ability of devices to support modularity. Devices with a fixed type/number of interfaces would not support growth. Redundancy is an important factor, but typically found in large enterprises. Network monitoring is also an important consideration, but not as important as modularity.<br />
</p></div></li>
<p></p>
<li><strong>Which network design consideration would be more important to a large corporation than to a small business?</strong>
<ul>
<li>Internet router</li>
<li>firewall</li>
<li>low port density switch</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>redundancy*</strong></span></li>
</ul>
<p><div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
Small businesses today do need Internet access and use an Internet router to provide this need. A switch is required to connect the two host devices and any IP phones or network devices such as a printer or a scanner. The switch may be integrated into the router. A firewall is needed to protect the business computing assets. Redundancy is not normally found in very small companies, but slightly larger small companies might use port density redundancy or have redundant Internet providers/links.<br />
</p></div></li>
<p></p>
<li><strong>Which two traffic types require delay sensitive delivery? (Choose two.)</strong>
<ul>
<li>email</li>
<li>web</li>
<li>FTP</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>voice*</strong></span></li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>video*</strong></span></li>
</ul>
<p><div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
Voice and video traffic have delay sensitive characteristics and must be given priority over other traffic types such as web, email, and file transfer traffic.<br />
</p></div></li>
<p></p>
<li><strong>A network administrator for a small company is contemplating how to scale the network over the next three years to accommodate projected growth. Which three types of information should be used to plan for network growth? (Choose three.)</strong>
<ul>
<li>human resource policies and procedures for all employees in the company</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>documentation of the current physical and logical topologies *</strong></span></li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>analysis of the network traffic based on protocols, applications, and services used on the network*</strong></span></li>
<li>history and mission statement of the company</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>inventory of the devices that are currently used on the network*</strong></span></li>
<li>listing of the current employees and their role in the company</li>
</ul>
<p><div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
Several elements that are needed to scale a network include documentation of the physical and logical topology, a list of devices that are used on the network, and an analysis of the traffic on the network.<br />
</p></div></li>
<p></p>
<li><strong>Which two statements describe how to assess traffic flow patterns and network traffic types using a protocol analyzer? (Choose two.)</strong>
<ul>
<li>Capture traffic on the weekends when most employees are off work.</li>
<li>Only capture traffic in the areas of the network that receive most of the traffic such as the data center.</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>Capture traffic during peak utilization times to get a good representation of the different traffic types. *</strong></span></li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>Perform the capture on different network segments.*</strong></span></li>
<li>Only capture WAN traffic because traffic to the web is responsible for the largest amount of traffic on a network.</li>
</ul>
<p><div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
Traffic flow patterns should be gathered during peak utilization times to get a good representation of the different traffic types. The capture should also be performed on different network segments because some traffic will be local to a particular segment.<br />
</p></div></li>
<p></p>
<li><strong>Some routers and switches in a wiring closet malfunctioned after an air conditioning unit failed. What type of threat does this situation describe?</strong>
<ul>
<li>configuration</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>environmental*</strong></span></li>
<li>electrical</li>
<li>maintenance</li>
</ul>
<p><div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
The four classes of threats are as follows:<br />
Hardware threats &#8211; physical damage to servers, routers, switches, cabling plant, and workstations<br />
Environmental threats &#8211; temperature extremes (too hot or too cold) or humidity extremes (too wet or too dry)<br />
Electrical threats &#8211; voltage spikes, insufficient supply voltage (brownouts), unconditioned power (noise), and total power loss<br />
Maintenance threats &#8211; poor handling of key electrical components (electrostatic discharge), lack of critical spare parts, poor cabling, and poor labeling<br />
</p></div></li>
<p></p>
<li><strong>Which type of network threat is intended to prevent authorized users from accessing resources?</strong>
<ul>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>DoS attacks*</strong></span></li>
<li>access attacks</li>
<li>reconnaissance attacks</li>
<li>trust exploitation</li>
</ul>
<p><div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
Network reconnaissance attacks involve the unauthorized discovery and mapping of the network and network systems. Access attacks and trust exploitation involve unauthorized manipulation of data and access to systems or user privileges. DoS, or Denial of Service attacks, are intended to prevent legitimate users and devices from accessing network resources.<br />
</p></div></li>
<p></p>
<li><strong>Which two actions can be taken to prevent a successful network attack on an email server account? (Choose two.)</strong>
<ul>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>Never send the password through the network in a clear text.*</strong></span></li>
<li>Never use passwords that need the Shift key.</li>
<li>Use servers from different vendors.</li>
<li>Distribute servers throughout the building, placing them close to the stakeholders.</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>Limit the number of unsuccessful attempts to log in to the server.*</strong></span></li>
</ul>
<p><div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
One of the most common types of access attack uses a packet sniffer to yield user accounts and passwords that are transmitted as clear text. Repeated attempts to log in to a server to gain unauthorized access constitute another type of access attack. Limiting the number of attempts to log in to the server and using encrypted passwords will help prevent successful logins through these types of access attack.<br />
</p></div></li>
<p></p>
<li><strong>Which firewall feature is used to ensure that packets coming into a network are legitimate responses initiated from internal hosts?</strong>
<ul>
<li>application filtering</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>stateful packet inspection*</strong></span></li>
<li>URL filtering</li>
<li>packet filtering</li>
</ul>
<p><div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
Stateful packet inspection on a firewall checks that incoming packets are actually legitimate responses to requests originating from hosts inside the network. Packet filtering can be used to permit or deny access to resources based on IP or MAC address. Application filtering can permit or deny access based on port number. URL filtering is used to permit or deny access based on URL or on keywords.<br />
</p></div></li>
<p></p>
<li><strong>What is the purpose of the network security authentication function?</strong>
<ul>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>to require users to prove who they are*</strong></span></li>
<li>to determine which resources a user can access</li>
<li>to keep track of the actions of a user</li>
<li>to provide challenge and response questions</li>
</ul>
<p><div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
Authentication, authorization, and accounting are network services collectively known as AAA. Authentication requires users to prove who they are. Authorization determines which resources the user can access. Accounting keeps track of the actions of the user.<br />
</p></div></li>
<p></p>
<li><strong>A network administrator is issuing the login block-for 180 attempts 2 within 30 command on a router. Which threat is the network administrator trying to prevent?</strong>
<ul>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>a user who is trying to guess a password to access the router*</strong></span></li>
<li>a worm that is attempting to access another part of the network</li>
<li>an unidentified individual who is trying to access the network equipment room</li>
<li>a device that is trying to inspect the traffic on a link</li>
</ul>
<p><div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
The login block-for 180 attempts 2 within 30 command will cause the device to block authentication after 2 unsuccessful attempts within 30 seconds for a duration of 180 seconds. A device inspecting the traffic on a link has nothing to do with the router. The router configuration cannot prevent unauthorized access to the equipment room. A worm would not attempt to access the router to propagate to another part of the network.<br />
</p></div></li>
<p></p>
<li><strong>Which two steps are required before SSH can be enabled on a Cisco router? (Choose two.)</strong>
<ul>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>Give the router a host name and domain name.*</strong></span></li>
<li>Create a banner that will be displayed to users when they connect.</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>Generate a set of secret keys to be used for encryption and decryption.*</strong></span></li>
<li>Set up an authentication server to handle incoming connection requests.</li>
<li>Enable SSH on the physical interfaces where the incoming connection requests will be received.</li>
</ul>
<p><div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
There are four steps to configure SSH on a Cisco router. First, set the host name and domain name. Second, generate a set of RSA keys to be used for encrypting and decrypting the traffic. Third, create the user IDs and passwords of the users who will be connecting. Lastly, enable SSH on the vty lines on the router. SSH does not need to be set up on any physical interfaces, nor does an external authentication server need to be used. While it is a good idea to configure a banner to display legal information for connecting users, it is not required to enable SSH.​<br />
</p></div></li>
<p></p>
<li><strong>Refer to the exhibit. Baseline documentation for a small company had ping round trip time statistics of 36/97/132 between hosts H1 and H3. Today the network administrator checked connectivity by pinging between hosts H1 and H3 that resulted in a round trip time of 1458/2390/6066. What does this indicate to the network administrator?</strong><br />
<img src="https://ccnav6.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/05/i208090v1n1_208088.png" /></p>
<ul>
<li>Connectivity between H1 and H3 is fine.</li>
<li>H3 is not connected properly to the network.</li>
<li>Something is causing interference between H1 and R1.</li>
<li>Performance between the networks is within expected parameters.</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>Something is causing a time delay between the networks.*</strong></span></li>
</ul>
<p><div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
Ping round trip time statistics are shown in milliseconds. The larger the number the more delay. A baseline is critical in times of slow performance. By looking at the documentation for the performance when the network is performing fine and comparing it to information when there is a problem, a network administrator can resolve problems faster.<br />
</p></div></li>
<p></p>
<li><strong>When should an administrator establish a network baseline?</strong>
<ul>
<li>when the traffic is at peak in the network</li>
<li>when there is a sudden drop in traffic</li>
<li>at the lowest point of traffic in the network</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>at regular intervals over a period of time*</strong></span></li>
</ul>
<p><div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
An effective network baseline can be established by monitoring the traffic at regular intervals. This allows the administrator to take note when any deviance from the established norm occurs in the network.<br />
</p></div></li>
<p></p>
<li><strong>Refer to the exhibit. An administrator is trying to troubleshoot connectivity between PC1 and PC2 and uses the tracert command from PC1 to do it. Based on the displayed output, where should the administrator begin troubleshooting?</strong><br />
<img src="https://ccnav6.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/05/i210352v1n3_210352-1.png" /></p>
<ul>
<li>PC2</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>R1*</strong></span></li>
<li>SW2</li>
<li>R2</li>
<li>SW1</li>
</ul>
<p><div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
Tracert is used to trace the path a packet takes. The only successful response was from the first device along the path on the same LAN as the sending host. The first device is the default gateway on router R1. The administrator should therefore start troubleshooting at R1.<br />
</p></div></li>
<p></p>
<li><strong>Which statement is true about CDP on a Cisco device?</strong>
<ul>
<li>The show cdp neighbor detail command will reveal the IP address of a neighbor only if there is Layer 3 connectivity.</li>
<li>To disable CDP globally, the no cdp enable command in interface configuration mode must be used.</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>CDP can be disabled globally or on a specific interface.*</strong></span></li>
<li>Because it runs at the data link layer, the CDP protocol can only be implemented in switches.</li>
</ul>
<p><div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
CDP is a Cisco-proprietary protocol that can be disabled globally by using the no cdp run global configuration command, or disabled on a specific interface, by using the no cdp enable interface configuration command. Because CDP operates at the data link layer, two or more Cisco network devices, such as routers can learn about each other even if Layer 3 connectivity does not exist. The show cdp neighbors detail command reveals the IP address of a neighboring device regardless of whether you can ping the neighbor.<br />
</p></div></li>
<p></p>
<li><strong>A network administrator for a small campus network has issued the show ip interface brief command on a switch. What is the administrator verifying with this command?</strong>
<ul>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>the status of the switch interfaces and the address configured on interface vlan 1*</strong></span></li>
<li>that a specific host on another network can be reached</li>
<li>the path that is used to reach a specific host on another network</li>
<li>the default gateway that is used by the switch</li>
</ul>
<p><div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
The show ip interface brief command is used to verify the status and IP address configuration of the physical and switch virtual interfaces (SVI).<br />
</p></div></li>
<p></p>
<li><strong>A network technician issues the arp -d * command on a PC after the router that is connected to the LAN is reconfigured. What is the result after this command is issued?</strong>

<li>The detailed information of the ARP cache is displayed.</li>
<li>The ARP cache is synchronized with the router interface.</li>
</ul>
<p><div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
Issuing the arp –d * command on a PC will clear the ARP cache content. This is helpful when a network technician wants to ensure the cache is populated with updated information.<br />
</p></div></li>

<img src="https://ccnav6.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/05/2017-05-23_154756-1.png" /><br />
<strong>Place the options in the following order.</strong><br />
<strong>installing virus code to destroy surveillance recordings for certain days -&gt; <span style="color: #ff0000;">data loss</span></strong><br />
<strong>pretending to be someone else by using stolen personal information to apply for a credit card -&gt;<span style="color: #ff0000;">identity theft</span></strong><br />
<strong>preventing userd from accessing a website by sending a large number of link requests in a short period -&gt; <span style="color: #ff0000;">disruption of service</span></strong><br />

<strong>— not scored —</strong><br />

After an intruder gains access to a network, common network threats are as follows:<br />
Information theft<br />
Identity theft<br />
Data loss or manipulation<br />
Disruption of service<br />
Cracking the password for a known username is a type of access attack.<br />

<li><strong>Which term refers to a network that provides secure access to the corporate offices by suppliers, customers and collaborators?</strong>
<ul>
<li>Internet</li>
<li>intranet</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>extranet*</strong></span></li>
<li>extendednet</li>
</ul>
<p><div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
The term Internet refers to the worldwide collection of connected networks. Intranet refers to a private connection of LANs and WANS that belong to an organization and is designed to be accessible to the members of the organization, employees, or others with authorization.​ Extranets provide secure and safe access to ​suppliers, customers, and collaborators. Extendednet is not a type of network.<br />
</p></div></li>
<p></p>
<li><strong>A small business user is looking for an ISP connection that provides high speed digital transmission over regular phone lines. What ISP connection type should be used?</strong>
<ul>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>DSL*</strong></span></li>
<li>dial-up</li>
<li>satellite</li>
<li>cell modem</li>
<li>cable modem</li>
</ul>

<p></p>
<li><strong>Refer to the exhibit. An administrator is trying to configure the switch but receives the error message that is displayed in the exhibit. What is the problem?</strong><br />
<img src="https://ccnav6.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/05/i208399v1n1_Question-1.png" /></p>
<ul>
<li>The entire command, configure terminal, must be used.</li>
<li>The administrator is already in global configuration mode.</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>The administrator must first enter privileged EXEC mode before issuing the command.*</strong></span></li>
<li>The administrator must connect via the console port to access global configuration mode.</li>
</ul>
<p><div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
In order to enter global configuration mode, the command configure terminal, or a shortened version such as config t, must be entered from privileged EXEC mode. In this scenario the administrator is in user EXEC mode, as indicated by the &gt; symbol after the hostname. The administrator would need to use the enable command to move into privileged EXEC mode before entering the configure terminal command.<br />
</p></div></li>
<p></p>
<li><strong>Which keys act as a hot key combination that is used to interrupt an IOS process?</strong>
<ul>
<li>Ctrl-Shift-X</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>Ctrl-Shift-6*</strong></span></li>
<li>Ctrl-Z</li>
<li>Ctrl-C</li>
</ul>
<p><div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
The Cisco IOS provides both hot keys and shortcuts for configuring routers and switches. The Ctrl-Shift-6 hot key combination is used to interrupt an IOS process, such as a ping or traceroute. Ctrl-Z is used to exit the configuration mode. Ctrl-C aborts the current command. Ctrl-Shift-X has no IOS function.<br />
</p></div></li>
<p></p>
<li><strong>Refer to the exhibit. A network administrator is configuring access control to switch SW1. If the administrator uses Telnet to connect to the switch, which password is needed to access user EXEC mode?</strong>
<p> 	<img src="https://ccnav6.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/05/i275390v1n1_208237.png" /></p>
<ul>
<li>letmein</li>
<li>secretin</li>
<li>lineconin</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>linevtyin*</strong></span></li>
</ul>
<p><div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
Telnet accesses a network device through the virtual interface configured with the line VTY command. The password configured under this is required to access the user EXEC mode. The password configured under the line console 0 command is required to gain entry through the console port, and the enable and enable secret passwords are used to allow entry into the privileged EXEC mode.<br />
</p></div></li>
<p></p>
<li><strong>A network administrator enters the service password­encryption command into the configuration mode of a router. What does this command accomplish?</strong>
<ul>
<li>This command encrypts passwords as they are transmitted across serial WAN links.</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>This command prevents someone from viewing the running configuration passwords.*</strong></span></li>
<li>This command enables a strong encryption algorithm for the enable secret password command.</li>
<li>This command automatically encrypts passwords in configuration files that are currently stored in NVRAM.</li>
<li>This command provides an exclusive encrypted password for external service personnel who are required to do router maintenance.</li>
</ul>
</li>

<li><strong>What is the purpose of the SVI on a Cisco switch?</strong>
<ul>
<li>The SVI provides a physical interface for remote access to the switch.</li>
<li>The SVI provides a faster method for switching traffic between ports on the switch.</li>
<li>The SVI adds Layer 4 connectivity between VLANs.</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>The SVI provides a virtual interface for remote access to the switch.*</strong></span></li>
</ul>
<p><div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
The SVI is a virtual, not physical, interface that provides remote access to the switch. It does not impact Layer 4 nor does it enhance switching between switch ports on the switch.<br />
</p></div></li>
<p></p>
<li><strong>Which message delivery option is used when all devices need to receive the same message simultaneously?</strong>
<ul>
<li>duplex</li>
<li>unicast</li>
<li>multicast</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>broadcast*</strong></span></li>
</ul>
<p><div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
When all devices need to receive the same message simultaneously, the message would be delivered as a broadcast. Unicast delivery occurs when one source host sends a message to one destination host. The sending of the same message from a host to a group of destination hosts is multicast delivery. Duplex communications refers to the ability of the medium to carry messages in both directions.<br />
</p></div></li>
<p></p>
<li><strong>Which two protocols function at the internet layer? (Choose two.)</strong>
<ul>
<li>POP</li>
<li>BOOTP</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>ICMP*</strong></span></li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>IP*</strong></span></li>
<li>PPP</li>
</ul>
<p><div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
ICMP and IP both function at the internet layer, whereas PPP is a network access layer protocol, and POP and BOOTP are application layer protocols.<br />
</p></div></li>
<p></p>
<li><strong>What PDU is associated with the transport layer?</strong>
<ul>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>segment*</strong></span></li>
<li>packet</li>
<li>frame</li>
<li>bits</li>
</ul>
<p><div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
The PDU for the transport layer is called a segment. Packets, frames, and bits are PDUs for the network, data link, and physical layers respectively.<br />
</p></div></li>
<p></p>
<li><strong>What is done to an IP packet before it is transmitted over the physical medium?</strong>
<ul>
<li>It is tagged with information guaranteeing reliable delivery.</li>
<li>It is segmented into smaller individual pieces.</li>
<li>It is encapsulated into a TCP segment.</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>It is encapsulated in a Layer 2 frame.*</strong></span></li>
</ul>
<p><div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
When messages are sent on a network, the encapsulation process works from the top of the OSI or TCP/IP model to the bottom. At each layer of the model, the upper layer information is encapsulated into the data field of the next protocol. For example, before an IP packet can be sent, it is encapsulated in a data link frame at Layer 2 so that it can be sent over the physical medium.<br />
</p></div></li>
<p></p>
<li><strong>What type of communication medium is used with a wireless LAN connection?</strong>
<ul>
<li>fiber</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>radio waves*</strong></span></li>
<li>microwave</li>
<li>UTP</li>
</ul>
<p><div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
A wired LAN connection commonly uses UTP. A wireless LAN connection uses radio waves.<br />
</p></div></li>
<p></p>
<li><strong>In addition to the cable length, what two factors could interfere with the communication carried over UTP cables? (Choose two.)</strong>
<ul>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>crosstalk*</strong></span></li>
<li>bandwidth</li>
<li>size of the network</li>
<li>signal modulation technique</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>electromagnetic interference *</strong></span></li>
</ul>
<p><div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
Copper media is widely used in network communications. However, copper media is limited by distance and signal interference. Data is transmitted on copper cables as electrical pulses. The electrical pulses are susceptible to interference from two sources:<br />
Electromagnetic interference (EMI) or radio frequency interference (RFI) &#8211; EMI and RFI signals can distort and corrupt the data signals being carried by copper media.<br />
Crosstalk &#8211; Crosstalk is a disturbance caused by the electric or magnetic fields of a signal on one wire interfering with the signal in an adjacent wire.<br />
</p></div></li>
<p></p>
<li><strong>What are the two sublayers of the OSI model data link layer? (Choose two.)</strong>
<ul>
<li>internet</li>
<li>physical</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>LLC*</strong></span></li>
<li>transport</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>MAC*</strong></span></li>
<li>network access</li>
</ul>
<p><div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
The data link layer of the OSI model is divided into two sublayers: the Media Access Control (MAC) sublayer and the Logical Link Control (LLC) sublayer.<br />
</p></div></li>
<p></p>
<li><strong>A technician has been asked to develop a physical topology for a network that provides a high level of redundancy. Which physical topology requires that every node is attached to every other node on the network?</strong>
<ul>
<li>bus</li>
<li>hierarchical</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>mesh*</strong></span></li>
<li>ring</li>
<li>star</li>
</ul>
<p><div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
The mesh topology provides high availability because every node is connected to all other nodes. Mesh topologies can be found in WANs. A partial mesh topology can also be used where some, but not all, end points connect to one another.<br />
</p></div></li>
<p></p>
<li><strong>What type of communication rule would best describe CSMA/CD?</strong>
<ul>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>access method*</strong></span></li>
<li>flow control</li>
<li>message encapsulation</li>
<li>message encoding</li>
</ul>
<p><div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
Carrier sense multiple access collision detection (CSMA/CD) is the access method used with Ethernet. The access method rule of communication dictates how a network device is able to place a signal on the carrier. CSMA/CD dictates those rules on an Ethernet network and CSMA/CA dictates those rules on an 802.11 wireless LAN.</p></div></li>
<p></p>
<li><strong>If data is being sent over a wireless network, then connects to an Ethernet network, and eventually connects to a DSL connection, which header will be replaced each time the data travels through a network infrastructure device?</strong>
<ul>
<li>Layer 3</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>data link*</strong></span></li>
<li>physical</li>
<li>Layer 4</li>
</ul>
<p><div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
Because each data link layer protocol controls how the device accesses the media, the data link information must be removed and re-attached. Even if a packet is going from one Ethernet network to another Ethernet network, the data link layer information is replaced.<br />
</p></div></li>
<p></p>
<li><strong>What best describes the destination IPv4 address that is used by multicasting?</strong>
<ul>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>a single IP multicast address that is used by all destinations in a group*</strong></span></li>
<li>an IP address that is unique for each destination in the group</li>
<li>a group address that shares the last 23 bits with the source IPv4 address</li>
<li>a 48 bit address that is determined by the number of members in the multicast group</li>
</ul>
<p><div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
The destination multicast IPv4 address is a group address, which is a single IP multicast address within the Class D range.<br />
</p></div></li>
<p></p>
<li><strong>In an Ethernet network, when a device receives a frame of 1200 bytes, what will it do?</strong>
<ul>
<li>drop the frame</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>process the frame as it is*</strong></span></li>
<li>send an error message to the sending device</li>
<li>add random data bytes to make the frame 1518 bytes long and then forward it</li>
</ul>
<p><div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
Ethernet standards define the minimum frame as 64 bytes and a maximum of 1518 bytes. A frame less than 64 bytes is considered a &#8220;collision fragment&#8221; or &#8220;runt frame&#8221; and is automatically discarded by receiving devices. A frame greater than 1500 is considered a &#8220;baby giant&#8221;. A 1200 byte frame is within the normal range so it would be processed as is.<br />
</p></div></li>
<p></p>
<li><strong>What important information is examined in the Ethernet frame header by a Layer 2 device in order to forward the data onward?</strong>
<ul>
<li>source MAC address</li>
<li>source IP address</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>destination MAC address*</strong></span></li>
<li>Ethernet type</li>
<li>destination IP address</li>
</ul>
<p><div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
The Layer 2 device, such as a switch, uses the destination MAC address to determine which path (interface or port) should be used to send the data onward to the destination device.<br />
</p></div></li>
<p></p>
<li><strong>What will a Layer 2 switch do when the destination MAC address of a received frame is not in the MAC table?</strong>
<ul>
<li>It initiates an ARP request.</li>
<li>It broadcasts the frame out of all ports on the switch.</li>
<li>It notifies the sending host that the frame cannot be delivered.</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>It forwards the frame out of all ports except for the port at which the frame was received.*</strong></span></li>
</ul>
<p><div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
A Layer 2 switch determines how to handle incoming frames by using its MAC address table. When an incoming frame contains a destination MAC address that is not in the table, the switch forwards the frame out all ports, except for the port on which it was received.<br />
</p></div></li>
<p></p>
<li><strong>What are two features of ARP? (Choose two.)</strong>
<ul>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>If a host is ready to send a packet to a local destination device and it has the IP address but not the MAC address of the destination, it generates an ARP broadcast.*</strong></span></li>
<li>An ARP request is sent to all devices on the Ethernet LAN and contains the IP address of the destination host and its multicast MAC address.</li>
<li>When a host is encapsulating a packet into a frame, it refers to the MAC address table to determine the mapping of IP addresses to MAC addresses.</li>
<li>If no device responds to the ARP request, then the originating node will broadcast the data packet to all devices on the network segment.</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>If a device receiving an ARP request has the destination IPv4 address, it responds with an ARP reply.*</strong></span></li>
</ul>
<p><div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
When a node encapsulates a data packet into a frame, it needs the destination MAC address. First it determines if the destination device is on the local network or on a remote network. Then it checks the ARP table (not the MAC table) to see if a pair of IP address and MAC address exists for either the destination IP address (if the destination host is on the local network) or the default gateway IP address (if the destination host is on a remote network). If the match does not exist, it generates an ARP broadcast to seek the IP address to MAC address resolution. Because the destination MAC address is unknown, the ARP request is broadcast with the MAC address FFFF.FFFF.FFFF. Either the destination device or the default gateway will respond with its MAC address, which enables the sending node to assemble the frame. If no device responds to the ARP request, then the originating node will discard the packet because a frame cannot be created.<br />
</p></div></li>
<p></p>
<li><strong>Which two services are required to enable a computer to receive dynamic IP addresses and access the Internet using domain names? (Choose two.)</strong>
<ul>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>DNS*</strong></span></li>
<li>WINS</li>
<li>HTTP</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>DHCP*</strong></span></li>
<li>SMTP</li>
</ul>
</li>
<p></p>
<li><strong>What is a basic characteristic of the IP protocol?</strong>
<ul>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>connectionless*</strong></span></li>
<li>media dependent</li>
<li>user data segmentation</li>
<li>reliable end-to-end delivery</li>
</ul>
<p><div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
Internet Protocol (IP) is a network layer protocol that does not require initial exchange of control information to establish an end-to-end connection before packets are forwarded. Thus, IP is connectionless and does not provide reliable end-to-end delivery by itself. IP is media independent. User data segmentation is a service provided at the transport layer.<br />
</p></div></li>
<p></p>
<li><strong>Refer to the exhibit. A user issues the command netstat –r on a workstation. Which IPv6 address is one of the link-local addresses of the workstation?</strong><br />
<img src="https://ccnav6.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/05/i264448v1n1_264448.png" /></p>
<ul>
<li>::1/128</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>fe80::30d0:115:3f57:fe4c/128*</strong></span></li>
<li>fe80::/64</li>
<li>2001:0:9d38:6ab8:30d0:115:3f57:fe4c/128</li>
</ul>
<p><div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
In the IPv6 address scheme, the network of fe80::/10 is reserved for link-local addresses. The address fe80::/64 is a network address that indicates, in this workstation, fe80::/64 is actually used for link-local addresses. Thus the address fe80::30d0:115:3f57:fe4c/128 is a valid IPv6 link-local address.<br />
</p></div></li>
<p></p>
<li><strong>What is the valid most compressed format possible of the IPv6 address 2001:0DB8:0000:AB00:0000:0000:0000:1234?</strong>
<ul>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>2001:DB8:0:AB00::1234*</strong></span></li>
<li>2001:DB8:0:AB::1234</li>
<li>2001:DB8::AB00::1234</li>
<li>2001:DB8:0:AB:0:1234</li>
</ul>
<p><div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
There are two rules defining how an IPv6 address can be compressed. The first rule states that leading zeros in a hextet can be eliminated. The second rule states that a single :: can be used to represent one or more contiguous all zero hextets. There can be one and only one :: in an IPv6 address.<br />
</p></div></li>
<p></p>
<li><strong>At a minimum, which address is required on IPv6-enabled interfaces?</strong>

<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>link-local*</strong></span></li>
<li>unique local</li>
<li>site local</li>
<li>global unicast</li>
</ul>
<p><div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
All IPv6 enabled interfaces must at minimum have a link-local address. Other IPv6 addresses can be assigned to the interface as required.<br />
</p></div></li>
<p></p>
<li><strong>An IPv6 enabled device sends a data packet with the destination address of FF02::2. What is the target of this packet?</strong>

<li>all IPv6 enabled devices on the local link</li>

</ul>
<p><div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
FF02::2 identifies all IPv6 routers that exist on the link or network. FF02::1 is the target for all IPv6 enabled devices on the link or network.​<br />
</p></div></li>

<li><strong>Which statement describes a characteristic of the traceroute utility?</strong>
<ul>
<li>It sends four Echo Request messages.</li>
<li>It utilizes the ICMP Source Quench messages.</li>
<li>It is primarily used to test connectivity between two hosts.</li>

</p></div></li>
<p></p>
<li><strong>What is the usable number of host IP addresses on a network that has a /26 mask?</strong>
<ul>
<li>256</li>
<li>254</li>
<li>64</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>62*</strong></span></li>
<li>32</li>
<li>16</li>
</ul>
<p><div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
A /26 mask is the same as 255.255.255.192. The mask leaves 6 host bits. With 6 host bits, 64 IP addresses are possible. One address represents the subnet number and one address represents the broadcast address, which means that 62 addresses can then be used to assign to network devices.<br />
</p></div></li>
<p></p>
<li><strong>Refer to the exhibit. An administrator must send a message to everyone on the router A network. What is the broadcast address for network 172.16.16.0/22?</strong><br />
<img src="https://ccnav6.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/05/i271962v1n1_211100.png" /></p>
<ul>
<li>172.16.16.255</li>
<li>172.16.20.255</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>172.16.19.255*</strong></span></li>
<li>172.16.23.255</li>
<li>172.16.255.255</li>
</ul>
<p><div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
The 172.16.16.0/22 network has 22 bits in the network portion and 10 bits in the host portion. Converting the network address to binary yields a subnet mask of 255.255.252.0. The range of addresses in this network will end with the last address available before 172.16.20.0. Valid host addresses for this network range from 172.16.16.1-172.16.19.254, making 172.16.19.255 the broadcast address.<br />
</p></div></li>
<p></p>
<li><strong>Given IPv6 address prefix 2001:db8::/48, what will be the last subnet that is created if the subnet prefix is changed to /52?</strong>
<ul>
<li>2001:db8:0:f00::/52</li>
<li>2001:db8:0:8000::/52</li>
<li>2001:db8:0:f::/52</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>2001:db8:0:f000::/52*</strong></span></li>
</ul>
<p><div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
Prefix 2001:db8::/48 has 48 network bits. If we subnet to a /52, we are moving the network boundary four bits to the right and creating 16 subnets. The first subnet is 2001:db8::/52 the last subnet is 2001:db8:0:f000::/52.<br />
</p></div></li>

<li><strong>A technician with a PC is using multiple applications while connected to the Internet. How is the PC able to keep track of the data flow between multiple application sessions and have each application receive the correct packet flows?</strong>
<ul>
<li>The data flow is being tracked based on the destination port number utilized by each application.</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>The data flow is being tracked based on the source port number utilized by each application.*</strong></span></li>
<li>The data flow is being tracked based on the source IP address used by the PC of the technician.</li>
<li>The data flow is being tracked based on the destination IP address used by the PC of the technician.</li>
</ul>
<p><div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
The source port number of an application is randomly generated and used to individually keep track of each session connecting out to the Internet. Each application will use a unique source port number to provide simultaneous communication from multiple applications through the Internet.<br />
</p></div></li>

<li><strong>What three services are provided by the transport layer? (Choose three.)</strong>
<ul>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>flow control*</strong></span></li>
<li>encryption of data</li>
<li>path determination</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>connection establishment *</strong></span></li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>error recovery*</strong></span></li>
<li>bit transmission</li>
<li>data representation</li>
</ul>
<p><div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
The transport layer is responsible for tracking digital conversations between a source application and a destination application through the use of port numbers. Two protocols that operate at the transport layer are TCP and UDP. TCP can provide reliability by establishing a connection, maintaining flow control, and error recovery.<br />
</p></div></li>

<li><strong>An Internet television transmission is using UDP. What happens when part of the transmission is not delivered to the destination?</strong>
<ul>
<li>A delivery failure message is sent to the source host.</li>
<li>The part of the television transmission that was lost is re-sent.</li>
<li>The entire transmission is re-sent.</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>The transmission continues without the missing portion.*</strong></span></li>
</ul>
<p><div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
Most streaming services, such as Internet television, use UDP as the transport layer protocol. These transmissions can tolerate some transmission failures, and no failure messages or retransmissions are required. Such control measures would create noticeable disruption to the flow of data.<br />
</p></div></li>

</p></div></li>

<li><strong>An author is uploading one chapter document from a personal computer to a file server of a book publisher. What role is the personal computer assuming in this network model?</strong>
<ul>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>client*</strong></span></li>
<li>master</li>
<li>server</li>
<li>slave</li>
<li>transient</li>
</ul>
<p><div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
In the client/server network model, a network device assumes the role of server in order to provide a particular service such as file transfer and storage. The device requesting the service assumes the role of client. In the client/server network model, a dedicated server does not have to be used, but if one is present, the network model being used is the client/server model. In contrast, the peer-to-peer network model does not have a dedicated server.<br />
</p></div></li>

<li><strong>When a network administrator is trying to manage network traffic on a growing network, when should traffic flow patterns be analyzed?</strong>

<li><strong>What will be the result of failed login attempts if the following command is entered into a router?</strong>
<ul>
<li>login block-for 150 attempts 4 within 90</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>All login attempts will be blocked for 150 seconds if there are 4 failed attempts within 90 seconds.*</strong></span></li>
<li>All login attempts will be blocked for 90 seconds if there are 4 failed attempts within 150 seconds.</li>
<li>All login attempts will be blocked for 1.5 hours if there are 4 failed attempts within 150 seconds.</li>
<li>All login attempts will be blocked for 4 hours if there are 90 failed attempts within 150 seconds.</li>
</ul>
<p><div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
The components of the login block-for 150 attempts 4 within 90 command are as follows:<br />
The expression block-for 150 is the time in seconds that logins will be blocked.<br />
The expression attempts 4 is the number of failed attempts that will trigger the blocking of login requests.<br />
The expression within 90 is the time in seconds in which the 4 failed attempts must occur.<br />
</p></div></li>
<p></p>
<li><strong>Which two statements correctly describe a router memory type and its contents? (Choose two.)</strong>
<ul>
<li>ROM is nonvolatile and stores the running IOS.</li>
<li>FLASH is nonvolatile and contains a limited portion of the IOS​.</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>RAM is volatile and stores the IP routing table.*</strong></span></li>
<li>NVRAM is nonvolatile and stores a full version of the IOS.</li>
<p><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>ROM is nonvolatile and contains basic diagnostic software.*</strong></span></li>
</ul>
<p><div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
ROM is a nonvolatile memory and stores bootup instructions, basic diagnostic software, and a limited IOS. Flash is a nonvolatile memory used as permanent storage for the IOS and other system-related files. RAM is volatile memory and stores the IP routing table, IPv4 to MAC address mappings in the ARP cache, packets that are buffered or temporarily stored, the running configuration, and the currently running IOS. NVRAM is a nonvolatile memory that stores the startup configuration file.<br />
</p></div></li>
<p></p>
<li><strong>A user reports a lack of network connectivity. The technician takes control of the user machine and attempts to ping other computers on the network and these pings fail. The technician pings the default gateway and that also fails. What can be determined for sure by the results of these tests?</strong>
<ul>
<li>The NIC in the PC is bad.</li>
<li>The TCP/IP protocol is not enabled.</li>
<li>The router that is attached to the same network as the workstation is down.</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>Nothing can be determined for sure at this point.*</strong></span></li>
</ul>
<p><div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
In networks today, a failed ping could mean that the other devices on the network are blocking pings. Further investigation such as checking network connectivity from other devices on the same network is warranted.<br />
</p></div></li>
<p></p>
<li><strong>For Cisco IOS, which escape sequence allows terminating a traceroute operation?</strong>
<ul>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>Ctrl+Shift+6*</strong></span></li>
<li>Ctrl+Esc</li>
<li>Ctrl+x</li>
<li>Ctrl+c</li>
</ul>
<p><div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
Once a traceroute is initiated in the Cisco IOS, it can be stopped by issuing the Ctrl+Shift+6 escape sequence.<br />
</p></div></li>
<p></p>
<li><strong>Match the phases to the functions during the boot up process of a Cisco router. (Not all options are used.)</strong><br />
<img src="https://ccnav6.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/05/2017-05-23_183149.png" /><br />
<img src="https://ccnav6.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/05/2017-05-23_183149-1.png" /><br />
<strong>Place the options in the following order.</strong><br />
<strong>— not scored —</strong><br />
<strong>locale and load the Cisco IOS software -&gt; <span style="color: #ff0000;">phase 2</span></strong><br />
<strong>locate and load the startup configuration file -&gt; <span style="color: #ff0000;">phase 3</span></strong><br />
<strong>perform the POST and load the bootstrap program -&gt; <span style="color: #ff0000;">phase 1</span></strong><br />
<div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
There are three major phases to the bootup process of a Cisco router:<br />
Perform the POST and load the bootstrap program.<br />
Locate and load the Cisco IOS software.<br />
Locate and load the startup configuration file<br />
If a startup configuration file cannot be located, the router will enter setup mode by displaying the setup mode prompt.<br />
</p></div></li>

<li><strong>What three blocks of addresses are defined by RFC 1918 for private network use? (Choose three.)</strong>

<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>192.168.0.0/16*</strong></span></li>

<li>239.0.0.0/8</li>
</ul>
<p><div class="message_box success"><p><br />
<strong>Explain:</strong>RFC 1918, Address Allocation for Private Internets, defines three blocks of IPv4 address for private networks that should not be routable on the public Internet.<br />
10.0.0.0/8<br />
172.16.0.0/12<br />
192.168.0.0/16<br />

<li><strong>A network administrator is variably subnetting a given block of IPv4 addresses. Which combination of network addresses and prefix lengths will make the most efficient use of addresses when the need is for 2 subnets capable of supporting 10 hosts and 1 subnet that can support 6 hosts?</strong>
<ul>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>10.1.1.128/28</strong></span><br />
<span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>10.1.1.144/28</strong></span><br />
<span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>10.1.1.160/29*</strong></span></li>
<li>10.1.1.128/28<br />
10.1.1.144/28<br />
10.1.1.160/2810.1.1.128/28<br />
10.1.1.140/28<br />
10.1.1.158/26</li>
<li>10.1.1.128/26<br />
10.1.1.144/26<br />
10.1.1.160/26</li>
<li>10.1.1.128/26<br />
10.1.1.140/26<br />
10.1.1.158/28</li>
</ul>
<p><div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
Prefix lengths of /28 and /29 are the most efficient to create subnets of 16 addresses (to support 10 hosts) and 8 addresses (to support 6 hosts), respectively. Addresses in one subnet must also not overlap into the range of another subnet.<br />

<li><strong>Match the descriptions to the terms. (Not all options are used.)</strong>
<ul>
<li>Question<br />
<img src="https://ccnav6.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/05/2017-05-23_182500.png" /></li>
<li>Answer<br />
<img src="https://ccnav6.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/05/2017-05-23_182500-1.png" /></li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Place the options in the following order.</strong><br />
<strong>— not scored —</strong><br />
<strong>CLI -&gt; <span style="color: #ff0000;">users interact with the operating system by typing commands</span></strong><br />
<strong>GUI -&gt; <span style="color: #ff0000;">enables the user to interact with the operating system by pointing and clicking</span></strong><br />
<strong>kernel -&gt; <span style="color: #ff0000;">the part of the OS that interacts directly with the device hardware</span></strong><br />
<strong>shell -&gt; <span style="color: #ff0000;">the part of the operating system that interfaces with applications and the user</span></strong><br />
<div class="message_box success"><p><strong>Explain:</strong><br />
A GUI, or graphical user interface, allows the user to interact with the operating system by pointing and clicking at elements on the screen. A CLI, or command-line interface, requires users to type commands at a prompt in order to interact with the OS. The shell is the part of the operating system that is closest to the user. The kernel is the part of the operating system that interfaces with the hardware.<br />
</p></div></li>

<li>A ping from the host to 127.0.0.1 would not be successful.</li>

</ul>
</li>
<p></p>
<li><strong>What are the two main components of Cisco Express Forwarding (CEF)? (Choose two.)</strong>
<ul>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>adjacency tables*</strong></span></li>
<li>ARP tables</li>
<li>routing tables</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>forwarding information base (FIB)*</strong></span></li>
<li>MAC-address tables</li>
</ul>
</li>
<p></p>
<li><strong>Which subnet would include the address 192.168.1.96 as a usable host address?</strong>
<ul>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>192.168.1.64/26*</strong></span></li>
<li>192.168.1.32/27</li>
<li>192.168.1.32/28</li>
<li>192.168.1.64/29</li>
</ul>
</li>
<p></p>
<li><strong>When applied to a router, which command would help mitigate brute-force password attacks against the router?</strong>
<ul>
<li>exec-timeout 30</li>
<li>banner motd $Max failed logins = 5$</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>login block-for 60 attempts 5 within 60*</strong></span></li>
<li>service password-encryption</li>
</ul>
</li>
<p></p>
<li><strong>Which statement best describes the operation of the File Transfer Protocol?</strong>
<ul>
<li>An FTP client uses a source port number of 21 and a randomly generated destination port number during the establishment of control traffic with an FTP Server.</li>
<li><span style="color: #ff0000;"><strong>An FTP client uses a source port number of 20 and a randomly generated destination port number during the establishment of data traffic with an FTP Server.*</strong></span></li>
<li>An FTP server uses a source port number of 20 and a randomly generated destination port number during the establishment of control traffic with an FTP client.</li>
<li>An FTP server uses a source port number of 21 and a randomly generated destination port number during the establishment of control traffic with an FTP client.</li>
</ul>
</li>
